Since Russian troops invaded Ukraine in late February, Delfast\u2019s top priority has been to see its Ukrainian team of 30 safely evacuated from the most dangerous parts of the country.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n When not focusing on sales, marketing, R&D and customer support, Delfast\u2019s smaller team of seven employees based in Los Angeles has been pleading with U.S. politicians and the European Commission to supply Ukraine with anti-aircraft missiles and fighter jets that could help Ukraine gain back some control over its air space, and, hopefully, put a stop to this war.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Delfast\u2019s co-founders, Daniel Tonkopi and Serhiy Denysenko, say they have always believed in safeguarding the future. When they founded Delfast in 2014, originally as a delivery company, Tonkoply and Denysenko knew that providing couriers with green transportation options would be critical to the company\u2019s operations.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n \t \n\t\t \n\t\t\tThe most important thing for an entrepreneur, and in general for any leader, is to protect the team and be completely honest with them during a tough time.\t\t\t\t\t\t\tDaniel Tonkopi, co-founder of Delfast<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/span><\/p>\n The founders soon realized that a bike with the power, range and battery life their couriers needed didn\u2019t exist, and so they set out to build one. In 2017, backed by a Kickstarter campaign that saw the company raise $165,000, the startup began manufacturing a bike to fit its needs \u2013 one that promptly <\/span>won the Guinness Book of World Records<\/span><\/a> for the greatest distance traveled on an electric motorbike on a single charge.<\/span><\/p>\n More recently, the Delfast Top 3.0 e-motorbike <\/span>won Forbes\u2019 fastest e-bike of the year<\/span><\/a> in 2022 after the company announced some serious <\/span>upgrades to the vehicle during CES<\/span><\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n We spoke with Delfast\u2019s co-founders to discuss what it\u2019s like running a startup during a war, how the startup is considering breaking into new business verticals, and the importance of always having a Plan B.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n The following interview, part of an ongoing series with founders who are building transportation companies, has been edited for length and clarity.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n Note: Serhiy Denysenko\u2019s answers were translated from Ukrainian by a member of Delfast\u2019s team for TechCrunch.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n TC: Serhiy, you’re on the ground in Kyiv. What’s your day-to-day like?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. It\u2019s important to keep in touch and know that everyone is fine, or as fine as is possible right now.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Besides my work as a COO, I\u2019ve been helping with volunteering, getting supplies and medicine to people, and this is something that pretty much every Ukrainian is now doing. I had my family relocated to Hungary, so I feel more or less safe, and I\u2019m just trying to work as much as possible and do my best in every possible area, whether that\u2019s supporting the company or supporting Ukraine in general.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n How are you managing your team through this crisis? What\u2019s changed?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>We got used to working remotely during Coronavirus times, so we have our task tracker, where everyone can see his or her task. Every Monday, we have an online Zoom meeting. Previously we only had these meetings at the executive level, but now during the war, we are gathering all together, just to see each other\u2019s faces and ask how they\u2019re doing, how\u2019s everyone feeling. Just to talk with everybody.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n <\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" “Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. the robo-berry"},"content":{"rendered":" If you’ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that’s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren’t super good at because they tend to be… crushy. But this robo-berry<\/a> designed by Swiss researchers could usher in a new era of gentle, automated robo-pickers.<\/p>\n The secret to picking a raspberry is to grip it just enough to get purchase and then pull it downwards off the little stem, apparently called the “receptacle,” which seems backwards. Seems simple \u2014 and it is, but only our hands are among the most sensitive and finely controlled constructions in the universe, the culmination of a hundred million years of evolution, outdone only by (I suspect) raccoons.<\/p>\n Robots simply don’t have the senses necessary to figure out the perfect technique for picking a berry. But what if it could communicate with the berry to better sense the forces involved and avoid either a a brutal crushing or humiliating failure-to-detach?<\/p> <\/div>\n That’s what Kai Junge, a PhD student at EPFL in Switzerland, aims to accomplish with this “sensorized raspberry,” a silicone and silicon replica berry that provides feedback to the picking machine, allowing it to learn to pick faster and better \u2014 and cleaner.<\/p>\n “It\u2019s an exciting dilemma for us as robotics engineers,” said professor Josie Hughes, who worked with Junge on the project. “The raspberry harvesting season is so short, and the fruit is so valuable, that wasting them simply isn’t an option. What’s more, the cost and logistical challenges of testing different options out in the field are prohibitive. That\u2019s why we decided to run our tests in the lab and develop a replica raspberry for training harvesting robots.”<\/p>\n Apparently the hard part comes just at the moment of detaching, when the force needed to grip the berry on the receptacle suddenly becomes overkill as the object goes from solid to hollow.<\/p>\n The replica berry has a fluidic sensor that tells the system how much compression is being experienced by the silicone drooplets, allowing the control model to learn how to adjust its grip as if the berry itself is telling it how much is too much.<\/p>\n You can see the berry in action below:<\/p>\n <\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The team plans to present their work at RobotSoft in April. And once the raspberry question is decided, they may move on to other berries, tomatoes, grapes&#8230; even apricots. The future is looking fresh!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you&#8217;ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that&#8217;s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren&#8217;t super good at because they tend to be&#8230; crushy. -companies?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=8191"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292389,"date":"2022-03-31T11:55:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T18:55:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292389"},"modified":"2022-03-31T17:57:31","modified_gmt":"2022-04-01T00:57:31","slug":"all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination\/","title":{"rendered":"All eyes are on Swvl as it starts trading on a SPAC combination"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mass transit and shared mobility provider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swvl.com\/\">Swvl<\/a> went public today in <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its shares at $10 on the Nasdaq through a merger with U.S. women-led blank check company Queen\u2019s Gambit Growth Capital. The planned merger, which will see Swvl offer 20-30% of its total shares, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">announced last July<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Following closing, the combined company, now \u201cSwvl Holding Corp,\u201d will trade under GMBT and GMBTW today before switching to SWVL and SWVLW on April 1.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292389\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl is the first company launched from Africa and the second Middle Eastern company to list on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Anghami, an Abu Dhabi-based music streaming platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">did so in February<\/a> when it listed with Vistas Media Acquisition at a $220 million valuation.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/embed\/#?secret=CnJTROn2h9#?secret=Q5eMhyfACo\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl raised $121.5 million in private investment in public equities (PIPE) for this transaction<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), Teklas Ventures, Chimera, Agility, and Luxor Capital Group are some of its other investors. The company is currently valued at $1.5 billion.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February, one of its investors, Atalaya Capital, pulled out of the transaction. And in a filing, Queen\u2019s Gambit announced the termination of forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreements worth $100 million in SPAC shares and an extra $2 million via a private placement.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreement <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was done<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> with a group, and it was <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> access to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> capital,\u201d Queen\u2019s Gambit Capital founder and CEO Victoria Grace told TechCrunch when asked if the termination affects the deal.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIts termination doesn\u2019t affect the valuation of the company or anything around our fundamental deal, which is Queen\u2019s Gambit merging with SWVL, so the valuation [stays] the same,\u201d she said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors withdrawing their interests and dollars from SPACs is not peculiar to Swvl. It\u2019s a usual occurrence &#8212; for instance, when BuzzFeed went public last December, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\">94% of the $287.5 million raised by the SPAC <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was withdrawn<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> &#8212; particularly as the SPAC hype gives way in the face of an underperforming market and tighter regulation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite the seeming setback, there\u2019s good news for Swvl. <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to CFO Youssef Salem, the company has an <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional $600 million from proceeds and<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> committed equity facility with B. Riley Principal to access over the next few weeks if certain conditions are met, he said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Swvl was founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">Mostafa Kandil<\/a>, Mahmoud Nouh and Ahmed Sabbah in 2017. The trio started the company as a bus-hailing service in Egypt and other ride-sharing services in emerging markets with fragmented public transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Its bus-hailing services enable users to make intra-state journeys by booking seats on buses running a fixed route. Swvl offerings have expanded beyond bus-hailing services, though. Now, the company offers inter-city rides, car ride-sharing, and corporate services in the 10 cities it operates in across Africa and the Middle East.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The partnership between Swvl and Queen\u2019s Gambit came from a mutual interest from both parties<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While searching for a company to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">acquire<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl fit the blank-check company\u2019s criteria: strong business fundamentals, mobility and logistics (one of its core verticals), and an ESG ethos around women and affordable transportation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the other hand<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl &#8212; off the back of raising over $170 million in venture capital, expanding to over 16 countries across Latin America, Asia and Africa; hiring executives from Facebook, Uber and Optimus; and acquiring Shotl, Viapool and door2door &#8212; was on a quest for global dominance in the mobility space. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A SPAC with Queen\u2019s Gambit was the most suitable option for it from a financial standpoint, and both parties feel strongly about the sustainability angle around transport &#8212; Swvl claims it has prevented approximately 289 million pounds of carbon emissions since its inception.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to expand into several countries over the next six months, including Colombia, Mexico, South Africa, and the U.S. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the meantime, all eyes will be on the company\u2019s performance as it <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">officially<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> starts trading tomorrow in a cooling SPAC market and a generally unsettled public market.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThere\u2019s a softness in the market, but as long as the company operates and delivers results, <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">maybe<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> today, people don\u2019t pay attention to it, but they will in months ahead,\u201d Grace said about the worrying SPAC and public markets.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I think<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the market will change <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> like it always does and people go back to fundamentals at how we look at company\u2019s performances. For Swvl, they have been beating every single number that was ever presented to us. And that\u2019s what makes me super excited about this. And that\u2019s the type of target you want to partner with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/\">Almost everything you need to know about SPACs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Almost everything you need to know about SPACs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/embed\/#?secret=dbGVg33T0n#?secret=s9kBhwdIHM\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Mass transit and shared mobility provider Swvl went public today in a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems. /tc_video?tags=21691"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576814951,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/corporate-services\/","name":"corporate services","slug":"corporate-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576814951"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576814951"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":52630,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/dubai\/","name":"Dubai","slug":"dubai","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/52630"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=52630"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292372,"date":"2022-03-31T12:05:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T19:05:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292372"},"modified":"2022-03-31T13:58:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T20:58:42","slug":"microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings\/","title":{"rendered":"Microsoft acquires process mining vendor Minit to grow its automation offerings"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Minit<\/a>, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which of those processes are ripe for automation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Minit currently enables businesses to transform the way they analyze, monitor and optimize their processes. Minit\u2019s solutions have helped businesses gain deep insights into how processes run, uncover root causes of operational challenges and help mitigate undesired process outcomes,&#8221; Justin Graham, Microsoft&#8217;s general manager of process insights, wrote in a <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/blog\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-minit-to-strengthen-process-mining-capabilities\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Microsoft&#8217;s corporate blog. &#8220;[With Minit, our] customers will be able to better understand their process data, uncover what operations look like in reality, and drive process standardization and improvement across the entire organization to ensure compliance at every step.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft dipped its toes into process mining with the launch of new features in Power Automate in 2019 and the acquisition of Softomotive, an RPA software provider, a year later. But with Minit, the tech giant is doubling down on a software category that could be worth over $11 billion by 2030, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wfmz.com\/news\/pr_newswire\/pr_newswire_technology\/global-process-mining-software-market-size-value-estimated-to-reach-usd-11-096-7-million\/article_a95b3354-ec2f-5389-b761-e4dbbdadbb97.html#:~:text=According%20to%20research%20report%20published,forecast%20period%202022%20to%202030.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to a report from Polaris Market Research.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292372\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It wasn&#8217;t immediately clear whether the whole of the Minit team will join Microsoft &#8212; or, indeed, whether the company will remain spread across its current locations. (Minit is now headquartered in Amsterdam, with satellite offices in London and New York.) But CEO James Dening said that customers shouldn&#8217;t expect a change in the level of support they&#8217;re currently receiving.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are looking forward to what it means to become part of an industry leader like Microsoft and what that brings us &#8212; how we can use that scale and excellence to continue to deliver great solutions to our customers,&#8221; Dening wrote in a blog <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/blog\/microsoft-minit-acquisition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Minit&#8217;s website. &#8220;It has been a privilege to lead the company for the last year, and I\u2019m excited to continue my journey with the team, as part of what I consider to be the world\u2019s leading software company.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Microsoft spokesperson Zara Huang told TechCrunch that the Minit team will move into the\u00a0<span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> Process Insights team and that there will be &#8220;no change&#8221; to the current work location of Minit team members. <span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> is in early stages of determining how Minit will be integrated into its offerings, she said, and the companies will share more details when they&#8217;re available.<\/p>\n<p>Minit, which was founded in 2015 by Rasto Hlavac and had raised \u20ac10.3 million (~$11.40 million) prior to the acquisition, is one of an expanding number of startups developing process mining tools aimed at enterprise clientele. Process mining, also known as task discovery, involves spotting root cause workflow issues and bottlenecks by pulling data from systems including desktop, email apps and workflows. It&#8217;s a key part of robotic process automation (RPA), a technology that promises to automate monotonous, repetitive tasks traditionally performed by human workers while at the same time generating logs to identify potential cost savings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As Protocol&#8217;s Aisha Counts <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/microsoft-process-mining-minit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notes<\/a>, process mining has traditionally been done by system integrators who map out processes by analyzing manual workflows. Process mining software is designed to digitize the approach in a way that reduces the expense, time and effort involved.<\/p>\n<p>Underlining the appetite for process mining technologies, Celonis, a data processing company, earlier this week acquired Minit competitor Process Analytics Factory, which coincidentally integrates with Microsoft&#8217;s Power BI analytics platform. Just in the past several years, RPA vendor Automation Anywhere acquired process discovery and mining startups FortressIQ, Process Gold\\ and StepShot; Blue Prism released a task mining solution called Capture; and rivals including ABBYY and Kryon have expanded their process mining offerings.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/\">Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/embed\/#?secret=wqSRCOP7wQ#?secret=2NKiKfcj0k\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;You know the process space is hot when even Microsoft, with its vast resources, has to buy its way in. I\u2019m sure Microsoft is seeing the same trends that we saw, which drove the combination of FortressIQ and Automation Anywhere,&#8221; Pankaj Chowdhry, EVP of discovery at Automation Anywhere and formerly CEO of FortressIQ, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Customers are starved for process data to help them navigate their transformation journeys and any vendor that doesn&#8217;t have best-in-class process capabilities will find itself challenged to offer a compelling solution to their customers.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft&#8217;s Minit acquisition comes at a time when the broader business process automation industry, which remains <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/robotic-automation-is-back\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flush with cash<\/a>, heads toward general consolidation. SAP acquired German process automation company Signavio in January 2021, just before ServiceNow got into the RPA segment with the buyout of India-based Intellibot.io. IBM <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.ibm.com\/2021-04-15-IBM-to-Acquire-myInvenio-to-help-Organizations-Use-AI-powered-Automation-to-Better-Streamline-Business-Processes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquired<\/a> process mining software company MyInvenio in April. And Salesforce\u2019s MuleSoft and Microsoft followed suit with the purchases of automation tech providers <a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/08\/02\/mulesoft-acquires-rpa-provider-servicetrace\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Servicetrace<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/10\/22\/microsoft-acquires-clear-software-to-strengthen-process-automation-offerings\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clear Software<\/a>, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Process mining, discovery and task mining has seen a lot of transformation with many acquisitions in the last year. [It] now appears to be maturing as a market and becoming commoditized under major automation platforms,&#8221; Saikat Ray, Gartner senior research director, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Gartner sees an emergence of automation platform vendors offering process mining and task mining as embedded capabilities, along with RPA.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated at 4:15 p.m. ET, March 31, with quotes from Microsoft and Automation Anywhere.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired Minit, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which automation","slug":"robotic-process-automation","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449560943"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449560943"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576598619,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/rpa\/","name":"RPA","slug":"rpa","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576598619"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576598619"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":6,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/technology\/","name":"technology","slug":"technology","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/6"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292473,"date":"2022-03-31T14:10:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292473"},"modified":"2022-03-31T14:10:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:57","slug":"better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation\/","title":{"rendered":"Better learning through &#8216;complex dough-manipulation&#8217;"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/robotics-roundup-12\/\">focused on pizza<\/a>. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly straightforward platform onto which ingredients are added.<\/p>\n<p>I say \u201cfairly\u201d here because there are still complications. There\u2019s really no such thing as easy when it comes to building robots that can execute variations on a task at a large scale. Here it\u2019s the dough that presents the problem. Turning a soft and malleable ball of dough into a pizza crust is one of those things humans have figured out how to do efficiently, but it still proves difficult for robot workers.<\/p>\n<p>A team of researchers at MIT, CMU and UC San Diego set out to create what they\u2019ve deemed \u201ccomplex dough-manipulation.\u201d The system is separated into a two-step process, in which the robot must first determine the task and then execute it using a tool like a rolling pin. The system, <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2022\/robotic-deformable-object-0331\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">DiffSkill<\/a>, involves teaching robots complex tasks in simulations.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292473\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>MIT notes:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>A \u201cteacher\u201d algorithm solves each step the robot must take to complete the task. Then, it trains a \u201cstudent\u201d machine-learning model that learns abstract ideas about when and how to execute each skill it needs during the task, like using a rolling pin. With this knowledge, the system reasons about how to execute the skills to complete the entire task.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The researchers say the system outperformed those trained in the more traditional reinforcement learning model. \u201cOur framework provides a novel way for robots to acquire new skills. These skills can then be chained to solve more complex tasks which are beyond the capability of previous robot systems,\u201d says CSAIL grad student, Yunzhu Li.<\/p>\n<p>This is robotics, so the whole pizza thing is really an initial problem for a system designed to tackle a lot more tasks. The company points to the emerging field of eldercare robotics as a possible use going forward.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been focused on pizza. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly Cribs","url":"\/shows\/tc-cribs","attr":"","target":"","classes":[""],"description":"","object_id":1605180,"object":"custom","type":"custom","type_label":"Custom Link","children":[]}]},"entities":{"posts":[{"id":2287135,"date":"2022-03-21T12:01:46","date_gmt":"2022-03-21T19:01:46","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2287135"},"modified":"2022-03-22T06:36:25","modified_gmt":"2022-03-22T13:36:25","slug":"miruku-replacing-animals-with-plants-to-create-dairy-proteins","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/21\/miruku-replacing-animals-with-plants-to-create-dairy-proteins\/","title":{"rendered":"Miruku replacing animals with plants to create dairy proteins"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Miruku, a New Zealand-based foodtech company, is applying its molecular farming process to program plant cells to be mini factories for producing proteins and other molecules, like fats and sugars, traditionally made by animals.<\/p>\n<p>The company was founded in 2020 by Amos Palfreyman, Ira Bing, Harjinder Singh and Oded Shoseyov, who all have experience in either dairy or plant science. Its alternative dairy proteins technology is currently being developed in Miruku\u2019s labs and greenhouses with corporate and R&amp;D partnerships to scale and be implemented across geographies.<\/p>\n<p>Its approach involves breeding and engineering plant crops to turn their cells into dairy proteins, CEO Palfreyman explained. This is different from competitors in the space that are using techniques like precision fermentation, which brews dairy inside fermentation chambers, and recruiting animal cells outside of the animal itself to produce dairy building blocks in cultivation chambers.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287135\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>How Miruku is differentiating itself is by breeding new plant crops that grow real dairy building blocks directly in the plants themselves using the energy of the sun. In that sense, the company is producing proteins more efficiently than cows, thus cutting out the role of the cow to reduce reliance on animal agriculture and the consequent damage to water, soil and atmosphere.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"oLmYVehzwp\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/28\/sectors-where-new-zealand-startups-are-poised-to-win\/\">Sectors where New Zealand startups are poised to win<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Sectors where New Zealand startups are poised to win&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/28\/sectors-where-new-zealand-startups-are-poised-to-win\/embed\/#?secret=hnmzh1tL6j#?secret=oLmYVehzwp\" data-secret=\"oLmYVehzwp\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;Our protein ingredients will make dairy foods which not only taste and smell like real dairy, but which are also nutritional equivalents to dairy,\u201d he added. \u201cThey will help build and repair your body with the same amino acid building blocks that your body uses after you have enjoyed and digested a scrumptious cheese sandwich and they\u2019ll function like real dairy in the making and baking of delicious things like cheesecake or a fine pecorino cheese.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>One of the challenges in foodtech is to create enough proteins or feedstock or scaffolding to scale the company, and for Miruku \u201cthe challenge of programming a plant to express mammalian proteins in a way that retains their structure and function is actually quite a technical challenge,\u201d noted Palfreyman.<\/p>\n<p>He explained that scaling the plants will be straightforward: Once you generate a plant that expresses the target proteins, you then plant the seeds to scale production, whether it&#8217;s a handful of them in a greenhouse or hundreds of thousands of them in a field.<\/p>\n<p>Where it gets a bit complicated is the engineering and breeding for selected traits, which often requires a trade-off between energy use and expression levels. However, Palfreyman believes Miruku\u2019s use of computational biology and techno economic analyses to model optimum expression levels will address that side of the scalability equation.<\/p>\n<p>The company is still in development, but Palfreyman is targeting two to three years before Miruku will see its proteins used in the commercial market. But it will have prototypes and proof of concept sooner than that. He expects the first product to likely be a partnership with an existing food company to provide a protein component that the food company will roll out.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Still, Palfreyman touts Miruku as the first molecular farming dairy startup in the Asia Pacific region. It joins other companies around the world, like <a href=\"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/nobell-foods-raises-75m-series-b-to-introduce-cheese-made-from-plants-301342308.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Nobell Foods<\/a>, also doing molecular dairy farming, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/09\/competing-with-both-perfect-day-and-beyond-meat-chiles-notco-raises-85-million-to-expand-to-the-us\/\">NotCo<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/01\/founded-by-an-impossible-foods-and-google-data-scientist-climax-foods-raises-7-5-million-to-tackle-the-cheesiest-market\/\">Climax Foods<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/the-weeks-biggest-funding-rounds-faux-cheese-hunting-tech-talent-and-insurance-against-hackers\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Perfect Day<\/a>, tackling animal-free technology to take on an over $500 billion dairy market. We\u2019ve seen a number of them secure venture capital funding in the past six months:<\/p>\n<ul>\n<li aria-level=\"1\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/28\/better-dairy-slices-into-new-funding-for-animal-free-cheeses\/\">Better Dairy<\/a>, which is creating cheese using the precision fermentation model, raised $22 million in February;<\/li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/07\/the-every-co-grabs-175m-as-it-cracks-code-on-animal-free-protein-products\/\">The EVERY Company<\/a>, using plants to make eggs, grabbed $175 million in December;<\/li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/25\/perfeggt-plant-based-egg-alternative\/\">Perfeggt<\/a>, also making eggs out of plants, announced $2.8 million in November and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.eu-startups.com\/2022\/03\/berlin-based-perfeggt-closes-e3-6-million-to-crack-into-europes-growing-foodtech-market\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">extended its seed round<\/a> to $3.9 million this month; and<\/li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/02\/stockeld-dreamery-loves-cheese-so-much-that-it-raised-20m-to-make-it-out-of-legumes\/\">Stockheld Dreamery<\/a>, making cheese out of legumes, secured $20 million in September.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<p>Miruku was self-funded by its founders for its first 18 months, and now secured $2.4 million in seed funding. The investment was led by Movac and includes Better Bite Ventures, Ahimsa Investments and the Aspire Fund.<\/p>\n<p>This will enable the company to begin to \u201cseriously scale\u201d after finding what Palfreyman said were the right partners to help connect the company to customers and build on milestones for the next round, which he believes will take place in 2023.<\/p>\n<p>The new capital will be deployed in adding more technology staff, developing partnerships and speeding up its development programs. Miruku already doubled its headcount this year and Palfreyman expects to grow similarly every year.<\/p>\n<p>Miruku was able to gain early traction with big food companies that are working with Miruku to co-develop products. It will also begin running development programs across geographies, some related to environment and climate, while others will be about product types and partnerships with growers, formulators and brands.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt is fair to say we are still an early-stage company, but it is no less accurate to say we are progressing rapidly and gaining great traction with strategic partners close to consumer markets,\u201d Palfreyman added. \u201cInnovation and growth necessitate access to capital, and while we have only just closed our first institutional round, we expect a consequent growth raise in the not too distant future.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"5S0xyKtHmy\"><p><a takes in $95M in equity, debt to roll out lending for small businesses"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Felix Rodriguez\u2019s family is from the Dominican Republic, and he watched his aunts and uncles come to the United States and create their own businesses. However, he noticed that not all small businesses were on a level playing field when it came to bookkeeping and working capital.<\/p>\n<p>In 2018, after a career as a network engineer, Rodriguez and his wife, Glennys Rodriguez, began helping small and mid-sized businesses manage their finances, and after joining with Edwin Mejia, founded <a href=\"https:\/\/www.finally.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Finally<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThere are all of these apps, and with most solutions, the founder is expected to deal with the tools,\u201d CEO Felix Rodriguez told TechCrunch. \u201cWe want to help them automate their finances so they can have a strong grasp on their numbers and build a better community and company for everyone involved.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286827\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Originally called Back Office, Miami-based Finally is collecting data points on bookkeeping, invoicing, bill payment and payroll, and leveraging artificial intelligence and automation to put together a financial picture for their clients. Today, the company works with over 1,000 small business clients and is managing close to $2 billion of transactions.<\/p>\n<p>After hearing from clients that they want to tap into the capital markets, but find it challenging to rely on banks and credit cards, Rodriguez says the second step of Finally is to unlock a credit opportunity.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>In the works is an all-in-one product that starts with a corporate card and will add additional credit products with plans to make over $1 billion in credit available.<\/p>\n<p>To get that off the ground, the company secured $95 million in Series A capital that includes $11 million in equity and $85 million in a credit facility, which is going to be used for lending to SMBs. The round was led by PeakSpan, with participation from Active Capital, 500 FinTech, and GTMfund. Individual investors include GeoCities founder David Bohnett and SessionM founder Scott Weller. Clear Haven Capital provided the debt facility.<\/p>\n<p>In addition to the lending, the company is using the new funding on hiring, including expanding both the engineering and sales teams. Finally also recently brought on a head of lending and will also hire to support that side of the business.<\/p>\n<p>Finally is a SaaS platform so clients pick a package depending on the amount of apps they have and pay a monthly fee. With the credit product, it will be free, and the company will make money from the interchange and other fees associated with the credit card.<\/p>\n<p>In the past two years, Finally grew from 12 employees to now more than 100, and has experienced triple-digit revenue growth.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cBefore COVID, we were preaching that you have to know your numbers, and when COVID hit, they really had to know their numbers to get PPP loans and then apply for credit,\u201d Rodriguez added. \u201cAccess to credit is something everyone is excited about.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"fpaSaRJf06\"><p><a how to pitch them in Q1 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, gets its horn as capital continues to flow into e-commerce infrastructure startups"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">When much of the shopping shifted online during the global pandemic, startups developing software and other products to aid the transition began to garner attention from venture capital firms.<\/p>\n<p>We\u2019ve seen companies across the e-commerce infrastructure and enablement ecosystem pick up larger and larger rounds, and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.commerceiq.ai\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">CommerceIQ<\/a> is the latest to secure late-stage financing. The CEO is Guru Hariharan, who you might remember from retail analytics company <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2016\/02\/23\/where-are-they-now-startup-battlefield-company-boomerang-commerce\/\">Boomerang Commerce<\/a>, a Startup Battlefield finalist in 2014. He <a href=\"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/lowes-acquires-retail-analytics-platform-from-boomerang-commerce-300853043.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">exited the company to Lowe\u2019s<\/a> in 2019.<\/p>\n<p>Hariharan\u2019s background is in machine learning and e-commerce, and while working at Amazon, he said the goal was to take humans out of the equation in retail, and so his team built software, called Amazon Selling Coach, on how to interact with the brands.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286885\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>As people started to shift their purchases of items, from tools to toothpaste, to Amazon and other marketplaces, Hariharan wanted to start a company that would power where all of that money was going.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2286887\" style=\"width: 310px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2286887\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2286887\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/image003.png\" alt=\"Guru Hariharan, CommerceIQ\" width=\"300\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/image003.png 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/image003.png?resize=150,150 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/image003.png?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/image003.png?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/image003.png?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/image003.png?resize=96,96 96w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/image003.png?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2286887\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> CommerceIQ \/ Guru Hariharan, CEO of CommerceIQ<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>\u201cIf you look at the entire retail situation \u2014 buying products from a brand, the buy and sell sides need to be balanced,\u201d Hariharan said. \u201cI left to start the company to focus on building the sell side of the equation for brands to sell and interface with retailers on the buy side.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>CommerceIQ\u2019s retail e-commerce management tools automate and unify aspects, like category analytics and management of retail media, sales and operations, under one roof for brands. Customers can expect 18% growth in sales on average, he added.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"V5x26sKoP6\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2016\/02\/23\/where-are-they-now-startup-battlefield-company-boomerang-commerce\/\">Where Are They Now? Startup Battlefield Company Boomerang Commerce<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Where Are They Now? Startup Battlefield Company Boomerang Commerce&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2016\/02\/23\/where-are-they-now-startup-battlefield-company-boomerang-commerce\/embed\/#?secret=a1hqcC6nMS#?secret=V5x26sKoP6\" data-secret=\"V5x26sKoP6\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>The Bay Area-based company is now working with more than 2,200 brands, like Johnson &amp; Johnson, Kellogg\u2019s, Kimberly-Clark and Bayer, that are managing incremental sales, category market share and unit profitability through online retailers, including Amazon, Walmart, Target and Instacart.<\/p>\n<p>CommerceIQ closed on $115 million in Series D funding, boosting the company\u2019s valuation to over $1 billion. The latest capital infusion comes less than a year from a $60 million Series C round that happened in June 2021. It also gives CommerceIQ $175 million in total funding secured in the past 12 months and $196 million to date.<\/p>\n<p>The funding round was led by SoftBank Vision Fund 2 and includes participation from existing investors, including Insight Partners,Trinity Ventures, Shasta Ventures and Madrona Venture Group.<\/p>\n<p>As part of the investment, Priya Saiprasad, partner at SoftBank Investment Advisers, is joining CommerceIQ\u2019s board of directors.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cE-commerce penetration has risen at an unprecedented rate, and online channels are a strategic priority for large brands,\u201d she said. \u201cTraditional brick-and-mortar strategy doesn\u2019t transfer over to e-commerce, but the old way with spreadsheets and human-driven operations don\u2019t scale. CommerceIQ is the leading channel optimization platform enabling the largest brands to win in retail.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>In addition to the opportunity to work with Saiprasad, Hariharan said the driver for going after new funding \u2014 especially when its seed fund is still firmly in the bank \u2014 was seeing the $4.5 trillion retail industry at a massive inflection point. That included $1 trillion flowing via e-commerce and the industry as a whole advancing five years in a matter of 12 months during the global pandemic.<\/p>\n<p>With regard to the 1 trillion breakdown in e-commerce, Hariharan estimates about $150 billion is going through direct-to-consumer, while the other $850 billion is indirect-to-consumer, like Walmart, Target and Gopuff sites.<\/p>\n<p>That\u2019s why he believes now is the time to accelerate CommerceIQ. The company closed out 2021 with 106% year-over-year revenue growth, 113% growth in customers served and a 100% boost in employees globally.<\/p>\n<p>The company also grew in automations, delivering 215 million last year, up 70 million in one year. This year, Hariharan expects to deliver 500 million automations. Meanwhile, $1.1 billion is flowing through the software, up from $250 million last year.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"MVTfVCpxaP\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/19\/automattic-tc1-acquisitions\/\">Can social and e-commerce transform the future of the open web?<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Can social and e-commerce transform the future of the open web?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/19\/automattic-tc1-acquisitions\/embed\/#?secret=uAlmhfI17N#?secret=MVTfVCpxaP\" data-secret=\"MVTfVCpxaP\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>The new funding will enable CommerceIQ to accelerate its R&amp;D and M&amp;A activities, which Hariharan said will focus on potential opportunities to go deeper and broader into the vertical SaaS and also look at expansion into the Europe and Asia Pacific regions.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are being more opportunistic and throwing fuel on the fire, but we are raising to throw fuel on a fire that is already burning nicely,\u201d he added.<\/p>\n<p>The fire is indeed burning across the e-commerce infrastructure ecosystem, with companies announcing new funding practically daily.<\/p>\n<p>Talia Goldberg, a partner at Bessemer Venture Partners, told me that \u201cit\u2019s a great time to be in an e-commerce enablement business given the tailwinds and adoption.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cOne of the reasons it is an attractive space to invest in is that people pay attention to the power of the business performance and growth, but also it is just a huge market,\u201d she added. \u201cThere is a lot of opportunity to go around, and for some businesses, there will not be a winner take all, but a number of leading companies that will carve up the market in different ways.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/media.londonandpartners.com\/news\/london-helps-drive-global-demand-for-digital-shopping\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">London &amp; Partners and Dealroom.co<\/a> reported this month that $51 billion of venture capital was invested into U.S. digital shopping companies in 2021, up from $23 billion in 2020. Globally, that was $140 billion last year compared with $68 billion the year prior. It\u2019s certainly not slowed down. Here are just a few we\u2019ve seen just this month:<\/p>\n<ul>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Akeneo, focused on product experience and information management, brought in <a href=\"https:\/\/newsdirect.com\/news\/akeneo-announces-135-million-series-d-to-redefine-product-information-management-category-556968495\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$135 million in Series D<\/a> financing. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/03\/20\/akeneo-grabs-13-million-for-its-crm-of-products\/\">We profiled them previously<\/a>.<\/li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Intuitivo, an Argentina-based AI and computer vision startup, raised $7.8 million in a seed round of funding as it develops a one-on-one shopping experience, transforming any cooler or cabinet into a smart grab-and-go.<\/li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Canal, which has developed a connected commerce app so that brands can directly manage relationships with suppliers whose product they sell, raised a $22.5 million Series A and launched in the Shopify App Store.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<p>Meanwhile, Ryan Lee, co-founder and CEO of marketplace launch tool Nautical Commerce, said we likely will continue to see traction as commerce technology companies continue to shift to e-commerce enablement tools.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIncumbents are over 20 years old and built on aging infrastructure created before the smartphone and social media,\u201d he added. \u201cOver the next decade, we will have connected commerce and other tools to share your catalog everywhere buyers are.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"BrhAzmrISE\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/04\/4-trends-that-will-define-e-commerce-in-2022\/\">4 trends that will define e-commerce in 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, Expert jumps into home goods e-commerce"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"http:\/\/www.theexpert.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Expert<\/a> started out in 2021 as a way for anyone, regardless of budget, to get a one-hour video consultation with some of the top interior designers in the world. Now, buoyed by $12 million in Series A funding, the one-year-old company is expanding into e-commerce to become what co-founder Leo Seigal referred to as \u201cFarfetch for home.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>We profiled the company when it launched with a <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/19\/gwyneth-paltrow-invests-in-the-expert-a-video-marketplace-for-high-end-interior-designers\/\">$3 million round<\/a>, with Seigal saying at the time, \u201cWe were able to attract a crazy roster of designers partly thanks to co-founder Jake Arnold (who styles the homes of Katy Perry and Chrissy Teigen), who is so highly regarded in the industry, and partly due to a timeliness of offering which is far above anything that has been tried in the home space.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The Expert began with 60 designers, and a year later has over 140 designers advising thousands of clients across 50 countries. There are over 1,500 designers on the waitlist, with Seigal saying less than 1% become an \u201cexpert.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286154\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Providing access to celebrity designers is an avenue other startups are taking, too. For example, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/13\/intros-app-attracts-andreessen-seven-seven-six-kevin-durant-to-connect-celebrity-e-design-experts-with-those-seeking-advice\/\">Intro<\/a> raised $10 million last year to power its app offering 15-minute consultations with the likes of Rachel Zoe and Nate Berkus.<\/p>\n<p>Many of The Expert\u2019s experts average 147,000 Instagram followers, which helped to drive 85% of organic traffic in 2021, he added. In addition, it drove 35% in repeat transactions and over $5 million in revenue in the first 12 months.<\/p>\n<p>After realizing the spending potential of clients requesting the consultations \u2014 over 45% of the company\u2019s clients had furnishing budgets of over $50,000, and 33% over $100,000, Seigal noted that the logical next step in The Expert\u2019s road map was to expand into e-commerce to be a one-stop shop for home goods.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cOur clients wanted our designers to inform them how to spend their budgets, so we felt we were leaving money on the table by not having a way for them to purchase everything under one roof,\u201d he added.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>This new expansion, dubbed Showroom, will launch this summer with over 60 home brands, including Crate and Barrel, Apparatus, Schumacher and Waterworks.<\/p>\n<p>Showroom is not only gathering trade brands, big box brands, new, custom and vintage under one roof \u2014 in some cases for the first time \u2014 but also providing the first direct-to-consumer sales channel and third-party sales channel for many of these partner vendors, Seigal said.<\/p>\n<p>The new funding was led by First Round Capital with existing investor Forerunner Ventures participating along with Sweet Capital, Promus Ventures, Pentas Ventures, and a group of angel investors, including Jen Rubio, Jenny Fleiss, Liz Hamren, Neda Navab, Harry Hurst, Gwyneth Paltrow and Brigette Romanek. As part of the investment, Forerunner partner Nicole Johnson will join The Expert\u2019s board of directors.<\/p>\n<p>The Expert won\u2019t be warehousing home good items, but will utilize a drop-ship method. It just hired its 16th employee and will be deploying the new funds into additional hiring, technology development and marketing. Seigal expects to double the employee headcount by the end of the year.<\/p>\n<p>Next up, the company will be testing out a \u201cThe Expert Vintage\u201d site that will feature revamped vintage furniture from Europe.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"uihVvDQTf4\"><p><a Seigal","slug":"leo-seigal","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576995626"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576995626"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576995626"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576995626"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576995626"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2286137,"date":"2022-03-18T05:01:18","date_gmt":"2022-03-18T12:01:18","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2286137"},"modified":"2022-03-18T09:25:39","modified_gmt":"2022-03-18T16:25:39","slug":"sleek-wants-to-be-the-last-shopping-check-out-form-you-ever-fill-out","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/18\/sleek-wants-to-be-the-last-shopping-check-out-form-you-ever-fill-out\/","title":{"rendered":"Sleek wants to be the last shopping check-out form you ever fill out"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">One-click checkout continues to stretch out its moment, and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.onsleek.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sleek<\/a> is the latest startup to get in on the venture capital action, where similar companies like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/28\/ownit-helps-brands-sell-products-at-the-point-of-discovery-with-one-click\/\">Ownit<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/14\/online-checkout-bolt-decacorn\/\">Bolt<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/12\/checkout-com-raises-1b-round-at-40b-valuation\/\">Checkout.com<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/10\/nigerian-one-click-checkout-platform-ourpass-raises-1m-pre-seed-wants-to-build-fast-for-africa\/\">OurPass<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/rapyd-raises-300m-on-a-2-5b-valuation-to-boost-its-fintech-as-a-service-api\/\">Rapyd<\/a> have collectively raised over $3 billion in investments within the past 18 months.<\/p>\n<p>Toronto-based Sleek, which was part of Y Combinator\u2019s summer 2021 batch, is developing a browser extension enabling one-click checkout and cash-back savings.<\/p>\n<p>It raised $1.7 million in a round backed by YC, Hyde Park Venture Partners, Fiat Ventures, Goodwater Capital, and a group of angel investors that includes Twitch co-founder Kevin Lin, Tribe Capital founder Arjun Sethi, Forge co-founder Samvit Ramadurgam, and Kyle Daley, a member of the Chime founding team.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286137\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Adam MacEachern started the company with his college roommates, Daniel Baum and Palmer McCutcheon, in 2021. At the time, they were looking at the web browser and building financial rails for the browser that would work everywhere, not just on one certain shopping experience.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cLife happens online, but nothing harmonizes it,\u201d MacEachern told TechCrunch. \u201cCheckout has inconsistent offerings, so we are building a one-click checkout that works everywhere for everyone. In the near future, no one will be filling out forms, and we want to be the one making that change.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Here\u2019s how it works: You install Sleek on your web browser \u2014 currently it is in the Chrome Web Store \u2014 and create your profile, adding your credit card. Then you simply shop online, and when you are ready to check out, you can pay with Sleek and earn up to 25% cash back for purchases on top of rewards for shopping.<\/p>\n<p>The product is still in private beta with thousands of individuals on the waitlist, and MacEachern expects to go public with Sleek by the end of the year. Despite not being public yet, the company has been driving revenue from day one, having secured over 1,000 retailers as it aims to grow its engineering team and customer acquisitions with the new funding.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Sleek makes money from its retail partners when a user checks out, keeping a small fraction as revenue and passing the rest on to users as the cash-back portion of its offerings. Some of the retailers already secured include Walmart, Macy\u2019s and Booking.com, and MacEachern estimates that Sleek can increase cart conversion, especially as over 70% of carts are typically abandoned.<\/p>\n<p>As mentioned, Sleek is among a group of companies going after a <a href=\"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/global-self-checkout-systems-market-trajectory--analytics-report-2021-301466724.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">global self-checkout system market<\/a> that is poised to be valued at $5.9 billion by 2026, up from $3.5 billion in 2020. And companies are working to find new ways to expand their footprint.<\/p>\n<p>This week, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.businesswire.com\/news\/home\/20220314005084\/en\/BigCommerce-and-Bolt-Deepen-Partnership-to-Embed-Bolts-One-Click-Checkout-and-Shopper-Network-Making-it-Available-to-Small-Medium-and-Enterprise-Merchants-in-the-U.S.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bolt and BigCommerce announced a partnership<\/a> enabling merchants of any size using BigCommerce\u2019s e-commerce platform to set up Bolt\u2019s one-click checkout in a self-serve manner in minutes.<\/p>\n<p>When looking at the landscape, MacEachern said people rely on embedding buttons on a site. However, Sleek believes embedding has a distribution barrier, which is why you don\u2019t see them working on every site.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cOur extension is powered by machine learning to navigate checkout the same way humans would,\u201d he added. \u201cWe are the browser level, so when they download Sleek, it is everywhere and works everywhere. That is the true experience of one-click checkout.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"cMukk1E1mp\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/23\/checkout-is-the-key-to-frictionless-b2b-e-commerce\/\">Checkout is the key to frictionless B2B e-commerce<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe aims to do for building design what Figma did for UI design"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https:\/\/arcol.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Arcol<\/a> is in the early stages of building a design and documentation tool that runs in your browser.<\/p>\n<p>Paul O\u2019Carroll started the company in January 2021 after being inspired by his father, who is an architect, and seeing the frustration he had with the lack of digital tools available to design a building. He recalls watching his father at a desk with pencil and paper, sketching out a building that would begin to come to fruition six months later.<\/p>\n<p>Prior to Arcol, O\u2019Carroll was at a digital design studio building design tools for large companies, usually with a building or architectural twist to it. He saw the technology being used was decades old and wanted to take on the legacy tools like Autodesk.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285675\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cThrough all of this I saw firsthand how bad the tools we use to design buildings are and I thought that architects, engineers and contractors deserved better tools,\u201d O\u2019Carroll told TechCrunch. \u201cWhat Figma has done in the user interface design space, we want to do in building design.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>You can catch more about Arcol\u2019s founding story in <a href=\"https:\/\/medium.com\/@PaulO_Carroll\/the-arcol-manifesto-fa59d9ec2354\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">O\u2019Carroll\u2019s blog<\/a>. The company is building web-based tools that can turn a 2D sketch into a 3D representation so that someone can design anything from a small building to a skyscraper using a creative and collaborative canvas.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The product is currently in development and will be released later this year, and O\u2019Carroll said the waitlist just passed 8,000 people. He said the technology is complex to build and the product will go into a closed alpha in the next few months and will roll out privately with 20 customers around May. By the end of the year, he expects to open it up publicly.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285678\" style=\"width: 270px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285678\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2285678 size-medium\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_4366.jpg?w=260\" alt=\"Paul O'Carroll, Arcol\" width=\"260\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_4366.jpg 1271w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_4366.jpg?resize=130,150 130w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_4366.jpg?resize=260,300 260w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_4366.jpg?resize=768,885 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_4366.jpg?resize=590,680 590w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_4366.jpg?resize=43,50 43w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 260px) 100vw, 260px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285678\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Paul O&#8217;Carroll, founder of Arcol. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Arcol<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>To keep the momentum going, the company raised $3.6 million in seed funding backed by Cowboy Ventures, Figma CEO Dylan Field, Figma head of corporate development and strategy Lauren Martin, John Lilly, Procore CEO Tooey Courtemanche, former Autodesk CEO Amar Hanspal and Packy McCormick. This gives the company just over $5 million in total funding after taking in $1.5 million in pre-seed funding last year.<\/p>\n<p>The new funding will be used to round out the leadership team and add to Arcol\u2019s team of five employees.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe need to build our product quickly because we have this peak frustration in the market,\u201d O\u2019Carroll said. \u201cFor architects, this was not happening and the creative aspect was lost. We want to bring back the magic.\u201d<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The company is building web-based tools that can turn a 2D sketch into a 3D representation so that someone can design anything from a small building to a
