O'Carroll","slug":"paul-ocarroll","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576995313"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576995313"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576995313"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576995313"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576995313"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":428212225,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/procore\/","name":"procore","slug":"procore","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/428212225"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=428212225"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=428212225"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=428212225"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=428212225"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2285728,"date":"2022-03-17T05:02:27","date_gmt":"2022-03-17T12:02:27","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2285728"},"modified":"2022-03-17T11:44:41","modified_gmt":"2022-03-17T18:44:41","slug":"melibios-seed-honey-production-minus-the-bee","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/melibios-seed-honey-production-minus-the-bee\/","title":{"rendered":"MeliBio\u2019s honey production, minus the bee, will have you buzzing"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https:\/\/www.melibio.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">MeliBio<\/a> is turning the 9,000-year-old method of honey production on its head, taking out the bee and injecting precision fermentation and plant science.<\/p>\n<p>Darko Mandich, a former bee-honey industry executive, and Aaron Schaller, a scientist and amateur chef, started the San Francisco-based company in 2020 with the goal of bringing sustainability to the $10 billion global honey market, which Mandich described as \u201cone of the most unsustainable agricultural sectors with broken supply chain and quality issues.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Mandich explained that his epiphany came while reading a <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wired.com\/story\/why-some-ecologists-worry-about-rooftop-honey-bee-programs\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Wired article<\/a> that reported on how keeping honey bees in bee hives was actually killing the 20,000 wild and native bee species due to the loss of a diversity in the bee population.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285728\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWe want to change the food industry in a way that we make food sustainable, nutritious and deliver it at no cost to our dearest animals, in our case, the bees,\u201d he told TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>There are some companies already working in the bee space, like Beewise, which is doing automated beehives using precision robotics, and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/06\/beeheros-precision-pollination-platform-wings-its-way-to-15m-in-new-funding\/\">BeeHero<\/a>, which is tracking the health of bees.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"EvqwsxnjV1\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/06\/beeheros-precision-pollination-platform-wings-its-way-to-15m-in-new-funding\/\">BeeHero&#8217;s precision pollination platform wings its way to $19M in new funding<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;BeeHero&#8217;s precision pollination platform wings its way to $19M in new funding&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/06\/beeheros-precision-pollination-platform-wings-its-way-to-15m-in-new-funding\/embed\/#?secret=E5Gz7zoy95#?secret=EvqwsxnjV1\" data-secret=\"EvqwsxnjV1\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Israeli company Bee-io is also working on a bee-free honey using patent-pending bio processes. However, Mandich touts MeliBio as being the first company to make real honey without bees. The product has been tested in four restaurants in New York with a successful outcome.<\/p>\n<p>MeliBio came up with two ways to make the honey without bees: the first is using plant science to understand how bees access the plants, and what they get from them in order to make the honey.<\/p>\n<p>Second, how to improve upon the molecular composition to scale and make the product. That is where precision fermentation comes in \u2014 by identifying the organisms that are good in this application so that it can be used widely, meaning in different ways from drizzling on food to baking with it.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The company has now raised $5.7 million in seed funding to help it expand into foodservice and business-to-business applications. In fact, MeliBio is already collaborating with 30 companies that have signed letters of intent to do validation studies, Mandich said.<\/p>\n<p>Astanor Ventures led the round and was joined by investors, including Skyview Capital, XRC Labs, Collaborative Fund, Midnight Venture Partners, Alumni Ventures, Big Idea Ventures and Hack Ventures.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285734\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285734\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2285734\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/MeliBio-Team-Media-Seed.png\" alt=\"MeliBio, Mattie Ellis, Aaron Schaller, Darko Mandich, Benjamin Mason\" width=\"1024\" height=\"575\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/MeliBio-Team-Media-Seed.png 1872w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/MeliBio-Team-Media-Seed.png?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/MeliBio-Team-Media-Seed.png?resize=300,168 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/MeliBio-Team-Media-Seed.png?resize=768,431 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/MeliBio-Team-Media-Seed.png?resize=680,382 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/MeliBio-Team-Media-Seed.png?resize=1536,862 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/MeliBio-Team-Media-Seed.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285734\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">MeliBio team, from left, Mattie Ellis, Aaron Schaller, Darko Mandich and Benjamin Mason. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> MeliBio<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are excited about MeliBio\u2019s approach in building a next generation food technology that connects plant science and precision fermentation,\u201d said Christina Ulardic, partner at Astanor Ventures, via email. \u201cDarko and Aaron are passionate about taking pressure off the commercial honey bee supply chain and consequently improving pollinator diversity. We are quite impressed by their first product.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The new funding will be deployed into further R&amp;D and scale-up of its microbial fermentation process and into the product\u2019s official launch in April. Mandich also wants to increase the number of full-time employees from four to 10 by the end of the year, which is in addition to 14 contractors.<\/p>\n<p>Though the company is pre-revenue, he believes that will change once the product comes out and MeliBio can focus on fulfilling the letters of intent from multibillion-dollar food companies and restaurants eager to work with them.<\/p>\n<p>Next, Mandich plans to look into the $500 billion ingredients market and how to leverage the company\u2019s precision fermentation technology to share the future of that market.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cBy using science as an alternative way, we reduce the pressure on wild and native bees,\u201d he added. \u201cThere is a rising demand for honey, but by making it our way, we help bee biodiversity. American companies import honey from all regions of the world, and that process is getting more complicated and the quality is not always guaranteed, meaning it might not be real honey. By making it here, we simplify the supply chain, and with a domestic supplier, there are no late deliveries or quality issues. MeliBio will produce honey in three shifts, 365 days per year and make it a price parity with honey on the market.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" founders about investors in the space<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, Mandich","slug":"darko-mandich","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576995333"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576995333"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576995333"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576995333"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576995333"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2285476,"date":"2022-03-16T09:53:56","date_gmt":"2022-03-16T16:53:56","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2285476"},"modified":"2022-03-16T11:14:22","modified_gmt":"2022-03-16T18:14:22","slug":"legal-tech-startups-bringing-law-order-to-fragmented-industry","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/legal-tech-startups-bringing-law-order-to-fragmented-industry\/","title":{"rendered":"Legal tech startups bringing law, order to fragmented industry"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">It\u2019s long known that the legal profession has not embraced technology as quickly as other industries.<\/p>\n<p>As a result, there are a number of legal tech startups eager to not only help lawyers, but automate some of the processes bogged down by pen and paper. Here, we take a look at two companies that recently secured funding, Justpoint and New Era ADR, to see their approaches.<\/p>\n<h3>Justpoint<\/h3>\n<p>Victor Bornstein, founder and CEO of <a href=\"https:\/\/justpoint.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Justpoint<\/a>, told TechCrunch that his company is leveraging artificial intelligence to create efficiencies for both prospective plaintiffs and attorneys, initially in personal injury. It is currently working with over 1,000 law firms.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285476\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Personal injury lawyers rely heavily on ads and easy-to-memorize 800 numbers to attract clients, but Justpoint believes that using data is a better tool.<\/p>\n<p>Here\u2019s why: The Boulder, Colorado-based company has collected over 300,000 historical claims and uses data extraction models to plug into a law firm to provide a score on how good the firm is at winning cases, like sexual assault, medical malpractice and product liability.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>That\u2019s one side. The second is equipping the firm with information on whether a certain claim is worth the law firm\u2019s time to take, mainly because of the time involved in diving into a case, plus the fact that firms often put up their own money initially to file lawsuits and obtain expert witnesses. Justpoint also brings medical expertise in-house to process the data and train the model.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cLawyers have an incentive,\u201d Bornstein said. \u201cA claim could receive $2 million, but if they settle quickly, it will save a lot of effort, though they will receive much less. We\u2019ve looked at how to make claims more efficient so lawyers can take a claim to the end instead of settling.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The company recently raised $6.9 million in a seed extension co-led by Divergent Capital and Charge Ventures. Additional investments came from Crossbeam Venture Partners, Honeystone Ventures, Interplay.vc, Weekend Fund, Turing co-founder Vijay Krishnan, Mainstreet co-founder Jackson Moses and Stonks founder Ali Moiz. It brings the total amount raised to $7.9 million.<\/p>\n<p>Justpoint makes money when the lawyer wins their case, which explains the company\u2019s incentive to send claims worth spending the lawyer\u2019s time on, Bornstein said.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThat puts a lot of work on us validating the claims,\u201d he added. \u201cIt\u2019s also why we are seeing an uptick in legal technology. Many firms are not interested in using technology, but this allows us to do the work for them. The way we see it is in 10 years, the legal tech space will bloom in a way we have not seen.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"1Xv6iHEGbu\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/05\/for-ma-success-tap-legal-early-and-often\/\">How to make sure your legal team is M&#038;A ready<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;How to make sure your legal team is M&#038;A ready&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/05\/for-ma-success-tap-legal-early-and-often\/embed\/#?secret=XyE7irbRHg#?secret=1Xv6iHEGbu\" data-secret=\"1Xv6iHEGbu\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<h3>New Era ADR<\/h3>\n<p>On the dispute resolution side, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.neweraadr.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">New Era ADR<\/a>, which launched in 2021, is going after a piece of the over $250 billion litigation and dispute resolution industry.<\/p>\n<p>Co-founder Rich Lee explained that legal disputes often take 18 to 24 months and hundreds of thousands of dollars to resolve. New Era is building a digital and virtual tool that cuts down on both the time and cost of resolving disputes by up to 90%. The company highlights risks so that companies and their law firms can reduce unnecessary litigation gamesmanship.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are taking the temperature down, reducing acrimony and refocusing litigation back on story-telling,\u201d Lee added. \u201cThe procedures in\u00a0court systems and current arbitration systems don\u2019t\u00a0lend themselves to fast, efficient resolutions, so we rewrote them.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>New Era manages all of the case intake, payments and scheduling and facilitates virtual meetings with arbitrators so that clients can get binding resolutions in as little as 60 days.<\/p>\n<p>The Chicago-based company recently raised $4.6 million in seed funding led by Nextview Ventures, with participation from Jump Capital. The company\u2019s original pre-seed investors, Motivate Ventures and Alumni Ventures, also participated in this round along with a group of individual investors, including David Kalt, Sean Chou, Pete Kadens and Lon Chow. This latest round gives New Era total funding of $6.3 million.<\/p>\n<p>New Era charges a flat fee per case, and in less than a year, was named as the dispute resolution platform in over 50 million contracts. So far in 2022, the company has already surpassed its 2021 revenue. Lee said the goal is to triple that in the next year.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"rZZILmHpcc\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/zero-systems-gets-12m-series-a-to-bring-automation-to-professional-services\/\">Zero Systems gets $12M Series A to bring automation to professional services<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Zero Systems gets $12M Series A to bring automation to professional services&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/zero-systems-gets-12m-series-a-to-bring-automation-to-professional-services\/embed\/#?secret=NCf4xaSn7r#?secret=rZZILmHpcc\" data-secret=\"rZZILmHpcc\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<h3>Continued investment in legal tech<\/h3>\n<p>Justpoint and New Era are among friends in raising capital to bring the legal industry into the digital age, with many of them also leveraging AI.<\/p>\n<p>Earlier this month, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/zero-systems-gets-12m-series-a-to-bring-automation-to-professional-services\/\">Zero Systems<\/a> brought in $12 million in Series A funding for its software that automates much of the manual workflow law firms handle every day. In February, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.yahoo.com\/now\/ex-parte-raises-7-5m-130000050.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Ex Parte<\/a>, a SaaS startup using AI to predict litigation outcomes, raised $7.5 million in Series A funding. Also, contract platform <a href=\"https:\/\/commonpaper.com\/blog\/meet-common-paper\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Common Paper<\/a> secured $4.5 million in seed funding.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThere\u2019s been growing enthusiasm for legal tech for a while now,\u201d Zack Hutto, director of advisory within Gartner&#8217;s legal and compliance practice, told TechCrunch. \u201cCorporate law spending is up 50% and we are projecting budgets will make a three-fold increase by 2025.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>He cited a September <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/legal-tech-venture-investment\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Crunchbase News report<\/a> that showed venture capital funding into legal tech topped $1 billion, which was a record amount compared to previous years.<\/p>\n<p>That was not something Hutto was surprised by, saying it was proof of all of the demand, which resulted in VCs wanting to grab a piece of the pie.<\/p>\n<p>He feels like the rise has been dramatic because it started from a small base. Corporate legal departments are spending millions of dollars, but are not using technology as much as you might expect. The legal profession was most insulated from technology and digital transformation, so the trend of startups coming in was bound to happen, though there is still some skepticism of how transformative those tools will be, Hutto added.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cPDF invoices do not give you the kind of insight to make better decisions around that spend,\u201d he said. \u201cOne-third of departments were using those in 2010, and fast-forward to the last couple of years, and that number has increased to around half of organizations using e-billing technology, but you still have to marvel at the fact that there is a large, unpenetrated market there.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"yayfXgFyKu\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/10\/22\/how-tech-companies-measure-legal\/\">How tech companies measure &#8216;legal&#8217;<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" fishes for restaurant partners to try plant-based salmon filets"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Alternative seafood startup <a href=\"https:\/\/plantish.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Plantish<\/a> believes it is close to initial distribution of its whole-cut salmon filet via restaurants.<\/p>\n<p>The Israeli company is only a year old, but has already tackled the structure of the whole cut, which is complex, co-founder and CEO Ofek Ron told TechCrunch. Its first product, Plantish salmon, mimics cooked salmon in taste, texture, appearance and structure, and has similar nutritional value of high protein and Omega-3.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cOver 70% of the seafood market is based on whole cuts, but alternative seafood now is mostly minced fish options like fish fingers and fried fish,\u201d he added. \u201cThat\u2019s how we are different. We are creating a new platform for the fish filet by deconstructing salmon to understand the molecules of it and then doing it with plant-based molecules.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285114\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Ron explained that the first generation of plant-based foods, which started about 20 years ago, was mimicking the taste. The second generation \u2014 where Beyond Meat and Impossible Foods comes in \u2014 were about both taste and texture. For the third generation, it is about structure and whole cuts.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"FKM8sPJcSt\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/14-climate-tech-investors-share-their-h1-2022-investment-strategies\/\">14 climate tech investors share their H1 2022 strategies<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;14 climate tech investors share their H1 2022 strategies&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/14-climate-tech-investors-share-their-h1-2022-investment-strategies\/embed\/#?secret=RO1JuFwxSa#?secret=FKM8sPJcSt\" data-secret=\"FKM8sPJcSt\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>He believes this will require more accuracy to build anything and that the fibrous structure will mean that the next generation of alternative protein companies will not be burger companies, but will be filet companies like Plantish.<\/p>\n<p>The company is not alone in this idea that whole cuts are the next wave. Also betting on it is Tender Food, which this week announced <a href=\"https:\/\/www.globenewswire.com\/news-release\/2022\/03\/15\/2403212\/0\/en\/Tender-Food-Raises-12-Million-Seed-Round-Led-by-Chris-Sacca-s-Lowercarbon-Capital-to-Scale-Production-of-Plant-Based-Whole-Muscle-Cuts-of-Beef-Pork-and-Chicken.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$12 million in seed funding<\/a> for its technology aimed at replicating whole muscle cuts, using plant protein, to make beef steaks, pulled pork and chicken breasts. Meanwhile, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/22\/can-100-million-get-wildtypes-cell-grown-salmon-into-the-wild\/\">Wildtype got $100 million<\/a> recently toward development of its sushi-grade salmon made from cell cultivation.<\/p>\n<p>Plantish has attracted its own funding, announcing today $12 million in seed funding, which Ron touts as \u201cthe largest seed round to date in the alternative seafood market.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>State of Mind Ventures led the round and was joined by Pitango Health Tech, Unovis, TechAviv Founder Partners, SmartAgro, E2JDJ, Alumni Ventures, FoodHack Syndicate and OurCrowd. The new funding gives Plantish a total of $14 million to date.<\/p>\n<p>Ron started the company in 2021 with Enviro founder Dr. Ron Sicsic, Dr. Hila Elimelech, whose expertise is in chemistry, bioengineering expert Dr. Ariel Szklanny and Eyal Briller, former director of product at Impossible Foods.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285374\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285374\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2285374\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Team-photo1-Photo-credit_-Or-Paravoznik.jpg\" alt=\"Plantish\" width=\"1024\" height=\"652\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Team-photo1-Photo-credit_-Or-Paravoznik.jpg 2169w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Team-photo1-Photo-credit_-Or-Paravoznik.jpg?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285374\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Or Paravoznik \/ Plantish team<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Unlike cell-cultured meats that are using animal-based cells to make food, Plantish salmon is using plant-based proteins and ingredients that are already being used in foods in the U.S. Therefore, the company does not need to get U.S. Food and Drug Administration approval to serve its food, Ron said.<\/p>\n<p>This is why he believes the company will be able to get pop-up locations up at the end of the year so people can try the product. Ron then aims to get Plantish salmon into the first five restaurants by December 2023 and to officially launch the product nationwide in restaurants by 2024.<\/p>\n<p>The new funding will enable the pre-revenue company to invest in R&amp;D and build a manufacturing facility for its machines that mix together relevant proteins and algae extractions so the salmon has the Omega-3 and necessary structure. The first machine will help get the food into those five restaurants, at which time the company will scale.<\/p>\n<p>Plantish\u2019s initial funding of $2 million was secured last year after drafting what the machine would look like and do, and now Ron says he and his team have proved out not only the technology, but have prototyped the product so that people can now try it.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are activists and are here to make a change,\u201d Ron added. \u201cWithin a few months of starting, we already had a prototype and could taste the salmon. We aim to change food tech from the inside and will do it as a mission-aligned company.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" foods","slug":"impossible-foods","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/287382922"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=287382922"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=287382922"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=287382922"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=287382922"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576601017,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/israeli\/","name":"israeli","slug":"israeli","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576601017"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576601017"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576601017"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576601017"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576601017"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":264561,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/meat-substitutes\/","name":"meat substitutes","slug":"meat-substitutes","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/264561"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=264561"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=264561"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=264561"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=264561"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2284964,"date":"2022-03-16T05:01:56","date_gmt":"2022-03-16T12:01:56","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2284964"},"modified":"2022-03-15T14:26:21","modified_gmt":"2022-03-15T21:26:21","slug":"loveseat-return-home-goods-marketplace","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/loveseat-return-home-goods-marketplace\/","title":{"rendered":"Loveseat gets comfy with new funding to expand its returned home goods marketplace"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Oversized items, like furniture, have become a common fixture at the curb in weekly trash days, with the Environmental Protection Agency finding <a href=\"https:\/\/www.epa.gov\/facts-and-figures-about-materials-waste-and-recycling\/durable-goods-product-specific-data#FurnitureandFurnishings\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">80% ends up being disposed of in landfills<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Companies like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/10\/16\/floorfound-is-bringing-online-return-and-resale-to-direct-to-consumer-furniture-businesses\/\">FloorFound<\/a> have found success in managing furniture returns, but hot on their heels is <a href=\"https:\/\/www.loveseat.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Loveseat<\/a>, which also wants to improve that landfill statistic through its unique approach of an online returned goods marketplace where furniture is auctioned off locally.<\/p>\n<p>Husband-and-wife co-founders Chris and Jenny Stanchak started Loveseat back in 2013 as a vintage furniture business in Los Angeles and San Diego. In January 2020, the company started having issues with securing inventory and decided to try doing truckloads of furniture returns, and when that worked well, pivoted the company.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284964\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWe just kept doing that over and over,\u201d Chris Stanchak told TechCrunch. \u201cThere was more engagement, more participants and a higher price point. And that made sense because people want more contemporary stuff, not furniture that is too used or old.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The pair have since moved to Austin and set up a marketplace there, while also continuing in LA, San Diego and Orange County.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"kLm4Oy6spb\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/10\/16\/floorfound-is-bringing-online-return-and-resale-to-direct-to-consumer-furniture-businesses\/\">FloorFound is bringing online return and resale to direct to consumer furniture businesses<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;FloorFound is bringing online return and resale to direct to consumer furniture businesses&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/10\/16\/floorfound-is-bringing-online-return-and-resale-to-direct-to-consumer-furniture-businesses\/embed\/#?secret=OOQaQPuad5#?secret=kLm4Oy6spb\" data-secret=\"kLm4Oy6spb\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Their mission is to eliminate waste in the returns supply chain, which Chris Stanchak estimates is a potential $30 billion market, where between 20% and 30% of items are returned.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285080\" style=\"width: 410px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285080\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2285080\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/chris-jenny1-e1647379540227.jpg?w=300\" alt=\"Chris Stanchak, Jenny Stanchak\" width=\"400\" height=\"276\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285080\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Chris and Jenny Stanchak, co-founders of Loveseat<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>\u201cRetailers don\u2019t like dealing with returns,\u201d he added. \u201cAs people shifted purchases online, there are more remorseful returns, and it has become a big problem because you can\u2019t just put it back in a box. The retailer has to send it back to the manufacturer, so our goal is to find a new home for it.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Stanchak calls Loveseat, which sells customer returns or overstock inventory, a \u201cliquidity machine.\u201d It typically sells over 90% of the new items that go up on the marketplace each week.<\/p>\n<p>Most of the items are 70% off on average, and as an auction, the items start at $10, Jenny Stanchak said.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe have weekly auctions, so our customers are sticky, and they come back every week because items are new,\u201d she added. \u201cIf you are the first person to check the auction at midnight, you can get an amazing deal. We have hundreds of people checking the auctions each week, and we will extend the auction timing if there are bids at the last minute to make it like a game. We end up having a 55% repeat rate on customer purchases.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Loveseat hasn&#8217;t had to do much marketing, relying mostly on word of mouth, and in its second month of the marketplace going live in Austin, the market was profitable, Chris Stanchak said.<\/p>\n<p>As such, the couple would like to expand its footprint in its current four markets and launch into others, so they went after a round of venture capital and raised $7 million in Series A funding to jumpstart that growth.<\/p>\n<p>The capital injection was led by Bessemer Venture Partners, with participation from a group of angel investors, including Gokul Rajaram, Gabriel Weinberg and Kal Vepuri.<\/p>\n<p>In addition to market expansion, Chris Stanchak expects to use the new funding to round out the leadership team and bring in operations, finance and inventory sourcing talent. He plans to be throughout Texas within the year and enter another state with ultimate plans of being nationwide. The company is also looking to bring the same auction model to electronics and apparel in the future.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, with every market profitable, the company itself is heading that way as well, Chris Stanchak said. The goal is to triple its revenue this year, which is a similar trajectory from previous years. He is also aiming for bigger results from its next market in terms of auction size and dollar values.<\/p>\n<p>Talia Goldberg, partner at Bessemer Venture Partners, said she doesn\u2019t typically invest in companies with inventory, but the more she dug into Loveseat, the more their model was attractive and answered concerns the firm had of retail-oriented models. And rather than be like Craigslist, the company\u2019s value proposition focuses on new inventory, which is what consumers want, she added.<\/p>\n<p>Goldberg called the Stanchaks \u201camazing\u201d and a \u201cgreat balance in terms of their skillset and ability to be scrappy over the past couple of years.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe company hasn\u2019t needed to invest in marketing, customer acquisition or retail stores,\u201d Goldberg added. \u201cOnce people see the value proposition, they share it and have a fun, gamified experience, which helps to move inventory. Other models have inventory on hand, but this is more scalable, they are able to do so in a way that leads to a model that is attractive and something we look for in a marketplace.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"RE2Ng5Ltl1\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/03\/05\/etsys-2-year-migration-to-the-cloud-brought-flexibility-to-the-online-marketplace\/\">Etsy&#8217;s 2-year migration to the cloud brought flexibility to the online marketplace<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" backs Rutter\u2019s goal of being \u2018Plaid for commerce\u2019"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Seven months after publicly launching its company, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.rutterapi.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Rutter<\/a> is back with a new capital injection, this time $27 million in a Series A financing round led by Andreessen Horowitz.<\/p>\n<p>We first met founders Eric Yu and Peter Zhou last year when the company <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/20\/rutter-comes-out-of-stealth-with-1-5m-in-funding-for-its-e-commerce-api\/\">raised $1.5 million<\/a>. They started off building a universal e-commerce API for reading and writing data so that tech customers can integrate with commerce platforms and access financial data points to offer loans, launch in new marketplaces and streamline inventory syncing for brand management.<\/p>\n<p>Today, Rutter has similar tools for accounting systems and payment processors, including Shopify, Amazon, WooCommerce, BigCommerce, PrestaShop, Quickbooks, Xero, Stripe and PayPal.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284250\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Toward its goal of being \u201cPlaid for commerce,\u201d Zhou said that Rutter\u2019s core focus is to end all of the fragmentation that exists for companies to plug into all of these channels.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWhat surprises people is that this is more fragmented than people thought,\u201d he told TechCrunch. \u201cWe offer a diversity of platforms and act as the glue that connects all of the commerce tools, platforms and products out there to all of the merchants and small businesses.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Also participating in the new round of funding are new and existing investors, including Comma Capital, Mischief Capital, Basis Set Ventures, Haystack, the Chainsmokers and a group that includes founders and executives of companies like Plaid, Modern Treasury, RedHat and Airwallex. As part of the investment, a16z\u2019s Kristina Shen is joining Rutter\u2019s board.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284252\" style=\"width: 1010px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284252\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2284252\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Rutter-Auth-Flow.png\" alt=\"Rutter\" width=\"1000\" height=\"631\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Rutter-Auth-Flow.png 1000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Rutter-Auth-Flow.png?resize=150,95 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Rutter-Auth-Flow.png?resize=300,189 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Rutter-Auth-Flow.png?resize=768,485 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Rutter-Auth-Flow.png?resize=680,429 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Rutter-Auth-Flow.png?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284252\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Rutter&#8217;s authorization flow. <strong>Image Vredits:<\/strong> Rutter<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The company is working with customers, including Ramp, Airwallex, Uncapped and Lenkie on the fintech side and e-commerce enablement companies, including CJ Dropshipping, Gelato, Shirtsy and Moonshot Brands. Rutter currently launches about five new integrations every month and has plans to support more than 100 integrations by the end of the year.<\/p>\n<p>Zhou plans to use the new funding to build out Rutter\u2019s team of 19 into 80 by the end of the year. He is also focused on product development, including building a data infrastructure layer for commerce and building more features on the fintech side.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are seeing so much demand and product being pulled out of our hands, so we need to scale with new people,\u201d Zhou added.<\/p>\n<p>Since the second quarter of 2021, the company has grown 10 times in revenue, and following the funding round last August has grown five times.<\/p>\n<p>Zhou says this sector of e-commerce enablement is \u201can open field right now,\u201d with a lot of demand and much of it unmet. Its closest competitor focuses on fintech and not e-commerce, but Rutter\u2019s long-term goal is not to be a full-stack fintech company, and instead a data layer for commerce, he added.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Yu said the company is adding more coverage on platforms and will be going deeper into integrations and use cases. So far, fintech is one of the main use cases, but the company is seeing others on the commerce side, including shipping, drop-ship and marketplaces.<\/p>\n<p>To bolster what the company is seeing there, new products and features in the pipeline will be about getting data fast and in real time, including a webhook-based system to notify customers on orders.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ascbVi07th\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/04\/4-trends-that-will-define-e-commerce-in-2022\/\">4 trends that services","slug":"financial-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/53015"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=53015"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=53015"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=53015"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=53015"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2284684,"date":"2022-03-15T08:37:24","date_gmt":"2022-03-15T15:37:24","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2284684"},"modified":"2022-03-15T11:36:47","modified_gmt":"2022-03-15T18:36:47","slug":"moonshot-brands-funding-acquisitions-e-commerce-aggregator","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/15\/moonshot-brands-funding-acquisitions-e-commerce-aggregator\/","title":{"rendered":"Moonshot Brands funding, acquisitions highlight change in e-commerce aggregator space"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https:\/\/www.moonshotbrands.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Moonshot Brands<\/a> today announced it secured $30 million in equity and $150 million in a credit facility that will be used, in part, to purchase assets from other e-commerce aggregators. Co-founder CJ Isakow said this was just the beginning of what he thought would be <a href=\"https:\/\/www.moonshotbrands.com\/blog\/moonshot-brand-research-report-the-aftermath-of-covid-for-ecommerce\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">further consolidation<\/a> in the crowded sector.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cA lot of funding announcements came out last year, and people were buying at the peak of COVID pricing, but now aggregators are starting to fail, and we are purchasing assets from some of them,\u201d Isakow told TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>The equity portion was led by Anthemis and included existing investors YC Continuity and Garage Capital. The credit facility is from Victory Park Capital. It now gives the company $180 million in total funding, Isakow said.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284684\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>He considers Moonshot Brands, which you can read more about in this <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/26\/e-commerce-roll-ups-present-the-next-wave-of-disruption-in-consumer-packaged-goods\/\">deep look into aggregators<\/a>, to be a boutique company, focused on Amazon and direct-to-consumer brands globally, and initially in the mobility and action sports sectors.<\/p>\n<p>However, Isakow doesn\u2019t much care for the \u201caggregator\u201d moniker. When he and co-founder Allan Fisch were getting started in 2020, they saw how similar companies, like Thrasio, were using debt capital to buy lots of brands and take them over. Instead, Isakow and Fisch wanted to be involved with entrepreneurs who would join Moonshot and run their own brands.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"atrQsBfapp\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/14\/korean-internet-giant-naver-backs-e-commerce-aggregator-new-vessel-in-seed-round\/\">Korean internet giant Naver backs e-commerce aggregator New Vessel in seed round\u00a0<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Korean internet giant Naver backs e-commerce aggregator New Vessel in seed round\u00a0&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/14\/korean-internet-giant-naver-backs-e-commerce-aggregator-new-vessel-in-seed-round\/embed\/#?secret=jM6vmaKcmW#?secret=atrQsBfapp\" data-secret=\"atrQsBfapp\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWe want to take them off of Amazon and don\u2019t want to just buy EBIDTA, but build long-term brands,\u201d Isakow added.<\/p>\n<p>The assets Moonshot purchased were from Product Labs and include scooter brand La Scoota and fitness brand WOD Nation. Moonshot has nine brands, including Magneto Boards, and is now positioned to grow to over $100 million in trailing 12 months growth by the end of 2022.<\/p>\n<p>Before you go thinking that Product Labs is failing, Brad Moss, co-founder of the company, told TechCrunch that the tech-enabled service company, started two years ago, was the company working behind the scenes with many of the aggregators, like Thrasio and 101 Commerce, to provide the software, data and other tools to build their brands.<\/p>\n<p>When Product Labs brought in external money, that led to the creation of a holding company which purchased several different brands. When the investment group decided to break up the assets, those brands, including La Scoota and WOD Nation, were sold, Moss said. He now runs the company part and merged it with another company called Brandless.<\/p>\n<p>E-commerce aggregators around the world still seem to be doing well and attracting venture capital. For example, in the past six months <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/14\/korean-internet-giant-naver-backs-e-commerce-aggregator-new-vessel-in-seed-round\/\">New Vessel<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/02\/e-commerce-aggregator-una-brands-raises-15m-series-a-five-months-after-its-launch\/\">Una Brands<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/07\/chinese-amazon-aggregator-nebula-brands-raises-50m-led-by-l-catterton\/\">Nebula Brands<\/a>, all in Asia, brought in new funds, as did <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/09\/e-commerce-aggregator-merama-gets-its-horn-after-just-12-months-in-business\/\">Merama<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/08\/quinio-jumps-into-world-of-e-commerce-aggregators-with-20m-seed\/\">Quinio<\/a> in Latin America. Meanwhile another aggregator, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/society-brands-raises-204m-led-by-i80-group-in-first-institutional-capital-raise-301499124.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Society Brands<\/a>, which also encourages founders to lead their brands, secured $204 million last week.<\/p>\n<p>And just today, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/12\/elevate-brands-banks-250m-to-roll-up-third-party-merchants-selling-on-amazons-marketplace\/\">Elevate Brands<\/a>, which acquires and operates Amazon fulfillment businesses, announced a refinancing and upsizing of its credit facility to $400 million, led by funds and accounts managed by BlackRock. This brings the company\u2019s funding total to $590 million and will enable Elevate to scale its portfolio to 45 brands, from 32, this year.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>However, the crowded nature of the sector over the past few years has led to talk of eventual consolidation, something Taliesen Hollywood says is starting to happen.<\/p>\n<p>The Hahnbeck director works on e-commerce M&amp;A and follows the aggregator market. He cites as proof recent deals, including <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/31\/olsam-raises-165m-to-buy-up-and-scale-consumer-and-b2b-amazon-marketplace-sellers\/\">Olsam<\/a> acquiring Flywheel Commerce and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/01\/berlin-brands-group-now-valued-at-1b-raises-700m-to-buy-and-scale-merchants-that-sell-on-marketplaces-like-amazon\/\">Berlin Brands Group<\/a> acquiring Orange Brands. He also pointed to an early deal in 2020 for <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/25\/thrasio-the-amazon-aggregator-raises-1b-in-fresh-funding-at-a-valuation-of-up-to-10-billion\/\">Thrasio<\/a> when it acquired Thirstii, which Hollywood believed was \u201cjust an efficient way for Thrasio to expand to Germany.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cMost of the aggregators are not in any urgent trouble though,\u201d he added. \u201cOn the whole their portfolios are doing OK on average, and the one thing most of their acquisitions have in common is very strong \u2014 above 20% \u2014 net margins. Even the ones who are paused will return to the market in a few months once seller expectations come back down.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Hollywood confirmed what Isakow said about buying in the peak of the market as one of the drivers to a change in the sector.<\/p>\n<p>Currently, he sees aggregators bidding fiercely for the most attractive assets, which is a small minority of the businesses they look at, and presenting much lower offers on the rest. On the seller side, he notes that they are expecting higher valuations than ever.<\/p>\n<p>In fact, he has heard some sellers are approaching aggregators and saying things like \u201cWe will only talk to you if you can guarantee us a 5.5-time multiple of seller\u2019s discretionary earnings before we even start discussions,\u201d Hollywood said.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cAggregators need to lower their average acquisition multiples \u2014 last year they wanted to \u2014 but we are getting a strong sense that now they need to,\u201d he added. \u201cSeveral of the aggregators are dealing with this by pausing acquisitions altogether. The rest are becoming much more cautious or highly focused on specific categories. Meanwhile their marketing and deal origination departments are still actively reaching out to sellers, giving sellers the impression that the market is still extremely buoyant. It will take a few months for this to normalize.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ZjDFDA24BC\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/26\/e-commerce-roll-ups-present-the-next-wave-of-disruption-in-consumer-packaged-goods\/\">E-commerce roll-ups are the next wave of disruption in consumer packaged goods<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" capital","slug":"venture-capital","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/202"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=202"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=202"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=202"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=202"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576894415,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/victory-park-capital\/","name":"Victory Park Capital","slug":"victory-park-capital","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576894415"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576894415"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576894415"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576894415"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576894415"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2284257,"date":"2022-03-15T07:01:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-15T14:01:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2284257"},"modified":"2022-03-15T10:06:40","modified_gmt":"2022-03-15T17:06:40","slug":"bobbie-50m-infant-formula","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/15\/bobbie-50m-infant-formula\/","title":{"rendered":"Bobbie drinks up $50M to expand infant formula product line"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Organic infant formula company <a href=\"http:\/\/www.hibobbie.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bobbie<\/a> is taking a hint from its staggering revenue results in 2021 to get out in front of its product pipeline.<\/p>\n<p>Laura Modi, co-founder and CEO of Bobbie, told me she had expected $4 million in revenue for 2021, but closed the year with $18 million.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt was pretty extraordinary,\u201d she told TechCrunch. \u201cWe had been heads down on growth and innovation, and what is clear is we have hit product-market fit. This is the product parents have been waiting for.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284257\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Modi and co-founder Sarah Hardy started the company in 2018 to develop a European-style infant formula manufactured in the U.S. At the time, Bobbie was the first new infant formula product to launch into the market in six years and was going after customers who were getting formula on the black market, Modi said.<\/p>\n<p>Its beginnings came with quite a big learning lesson. The company voluntarily recalled its product during its first year of operation due to product labeling errors found by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration. Modi <a href=\"https:\/\/milk-drunk.com\/bobbie-2019-fda-recall-approved-regulated\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">blogged about the recall<\/a> recently, and told me it was \u201cquite a humbling and harrowing journey.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2284280\" style=\"width: 410px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2284280\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2284280\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/LauraModi-Co-founder-and-CEO.jpg\" alt=\"Laura Modi, Bobbie\" width=\"400\" height=\"488\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/LauraModi-Co-founder-and-CEO.jpg 2527w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/LauraModi-Co-founder-and-CEO.jpg?resize=123,150 123w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/LauraModi-Co-founder-and-CEO.jpg?resize=246,300 246w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/LauraModi-Co-founder-and-CEO.jpg?resize=768,936 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/LauraModi-Co-founder-and-CEO.jpg?resize=558,680 558w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/LauraModi-Co-founder-and-CEO.jpg?resize=1260,1536 1260w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/LauraModi-Co-founder-and-CEO.jpg?resize=1680,2048 1680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/LauraModi-Co-founder-and-CEO.jpg?resize=41,50 41w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 400px) 100vw, 400px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2284280\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Laura Modi, co-founder and CEO of Bobbie. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Bobbie<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>\u201cWhen the world of regulation and disruption come together in one of the industries that is heavily regulated, there is zero room for error,\u201d she added. \u201cAnyone can pick up and recover, and that positions us in a strong place. It also taught me that women are bad-ass. To watch how we handled it with calm, humility and vulnerability, and then stood back up and said let\u2019s keep going. We were confident with what the product could do.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The infant formula market is poised to be a <a href=\"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/infant-formula-market-size-to-reach-usd-103-75-billion-by-2026--fortune-business-insights-300929520.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$103 billion market by 2026<\/a>. Bobbie isn\u2019t the only player in the game, but it is the only direct-to-consumer formula company currently, with Modi citing statistics that show 21% of parents plan to buy online in the next year. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cnn.com\/2022\/02\/08\/business\/baby-formula-shortages\/index.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Infant formula is going through a shortage<\/a>, currently, that was not helped by the <a href=\"https:\/\/www.fda.gov\/consumers\/powdered-infant-formula-recall-what-know\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">recall in February of Similac<\/a>, which has a large footprint of the infant formula market.<\/p>\n<p>We&#8217;ll have to wait and see what happens there, but Bobbie and others are filling the gap. On March 23, ByHeart\u2019s new infant formula brand will launch via its website and be priced at $39 for a 680-gram can, which is the equivalent of 46 four-ounce bottles.<\/p>\n<p>The company\u2019s formula was recently FDA-registered and is derived from its own manufacturing and R&amp;D using a blend of two proteins in breast milk. The formula is also touted as being the first in the U.S. to include organic whole milk.<\/p>\n<p>Both Bobbie and ByHeart received the Clean Label Project Purity Award and are certified as pesticide-free products.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"GYcNOl7HF5\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/19\/helaina-human-milk-baby-formula\/\">Helaina\u2019s latest round brings it closer to market with human milk-equivalent baby formula<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Helaina\u2019s latest round brings it closer to market with human milk-equivalent baby formula&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/19\/helaina-human-milk-baby-formula\/embed\/#?secret=zWv8DqsMX3#?secret=GYcNOl7HF5\" data-secret=\"GYcNOl7HF5\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Also in this space is Helaina, a company tapping into a precision fermentation process that programs yeast cells and teaches them to become manufacturing hubs to develop almost identical proteins found in human milk. It announced <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/19\/helaina-human-milk-baby-formula\/\">$20 million in Series A financing<\/a> last November and is currently working toward getting FDA approval and commercialization.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, even with that bump in the road with the FDA, Bobbie did indeed hit the ground running again. It raised <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/bobbie-bags-15m-series-a-to-create-a-better-baby-formula\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$15 million in a Series A round<\/a> last June and grew to 50 employees from 20 last year. Bobbie now serves over 50,000 parents in each state, and Modi expects the company to grow four times in revenue this year at a pace of about 60% month over month in growth that is not slowing down.<\/p>\n<p>When some investors began knocking on their door, Modi and Hardy saw an opportunity to invest now in the future of the company and its next generation of products that will take more than five years to come to fruition.<\/p>\n<p>So the company today announced $50 million in a Series B round that was led by Park West and included existing investors VMG and NextView and a group of over 100 new investors that are part of AirAngels, the Airbnb alumni syndicate.<\/p>\n<p>Modi was not able to reveal the company&#8217;s valuation, but she said it has tripled from where Bobbie was 10 months ago. The new round includes $40 million in venture capital and $10 million inventory debt and gives Bobbie a total of $72 million of funding to date, she added.<\/p>\n<p>The new funding will be deployed into those new formula products. It is also deepening its partnership with Perrigo, its manufacturing partner. Bobbie will also invest in product development and R&amp;D, which includes the launch of Bobbie Labs, a virtual laboratory that will fund infant feeding research and innovation.<\/p>\n<p>Bobbie is also thinking outside the box in terms of additional investment in the company. Last year, it created The MotherLode so that women and its customers could invest in a company that serves them.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ZgRTeAc1ki\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/26\/synthetic-biology-startups-ride-a-wave-of-investor-interest\/\">Synthetic biology startups are giving investors an appetite<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" thinks it shouldn\u2019t be so hard to collect lead-generation data"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Startups need data to grow, and <a href=\"https:\/\/hellopareto.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Pareto<\/a> CEO Phoebe Yao wants to make that as easy as possible.<\/p>\n<p>She started the company in 2020 to provide virtual data analysts for businesses. Pareto\u2019s team of data experts offer actionable insights for sales marketing and recruiting pipelines. That data can be anything from sourcing TikTok influencers to qualifying B2B sales leads, finding job candidates and researching NFT communities.<\/p>\n<p>Yao, who is a Thiel Fellow, was born in China and moved to St. Louis at a young age with her dad, who was a truck driver, and her mother, who was a nurse. She was initially interested in a career in classical music, but while applying for Stanford, her parents wanted her to go in a different direction.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2283533\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>She ended up being attracted to computer science, especially how the design of systems creates opportunities for people to access skill sets.<\/p>\n<p>While taking a gap year in college, she worked at Microsoft on designing a build-your-own virtual workforce focused on stay-at-home mothers, and it got her thinking about skill gaps, outsourcing and culture around working with companies from abroad.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThere was infrastructure in place for building the workforce, but what was missing was the culture around supporting skills development and turning that into meaningful career opportunities in technology,\u201d Yao told TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>She decided to start a bootcamp to train women to be virtual assistants, to analyze data and essentially be the right-hand person for an entrepreneur. Yao was in the middle of training 20 women when the global pandemic hit.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>She then decided to drop out of school and focus on the company, which was becoming a service startup founders would use. However, when she began to see patterns in projects more focused on data collection and processing, she and her team decided to pivot to leverage Pareto\u2019s operations teams to analyze data and build more technology to automate the process of data collection and analysis and to create a human-in-the-loop virtual analyst system.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe\u2019re on a mission to democratize access to quality data while empowering work at home moms around the world,\u201d Yao added. \u201cOur operations team is 100% women led and operated, and we\u2019re building world-class training and mentorship along with flexible remote work opportunities within a supportive community of peers.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Today, hundreds of businesses use Pareto, including Modern Fertility, Wander, Launch House and Pave.<\/p>\n<p>Yao\u2019s goal is now to scale the company and refine the business from a virtual assistant, which would be operationally intensive, to virtual analysis, which would be more technical, in order to deliver actionable data to customers. This is especially relevant as <a href=\"https:\/\/www.shrm.org\/resourcesandtools\/hr-topics\/behavioral-competencies\/global-and-cultural-effectiveness\/pages\/over-1-million-fewer-women-in-labor-force.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">1.1 million women were estimated to have left the workforce over the past two years<\/a> as uncertainly around education and child care continued during the pandemic.<\/p>\n<p>The company raised $600,000 in pre-seed funding in 2020, and today announced $4.5 million in seed funding that it closed in November. Investors include MaC Venture Capital, Seabed VC, Soma Capital, Fearless Fund, Liquid2 Ventures, Slope Agency and Thumbtack founder Jonathan Swanson. The new round gives Pareto $5.1 million in total, Yao said.<\/p>\n<p>The new funding is expected to last the company through the next few years, Yao said. The company plans to build out engineering and marketing teams to refine its product-market fit.<\/p>\n<p>Last year, Pareto had 40 team members on the operations team, and that has doubled in the past year. In that same time, monthly recurring revenue rose from $10,000 to $50,000, she added.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe plan to use the new capital to answer questions around product-market fit, figure out how much we charge for the product, long-term value and how to convert one-time customers into long-term customers,\u201d Yao said. \u201cBy allocating money to different questions and hypotheses, it will give us a soft metric for our Series A.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"EEmUfwSUak\"><p><a adds new funding into its cart to expand autonomous retail footprint"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Contactless stores are gaining traction, more so in Europe, but there are some trickling into the U.S., including Atlanta\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/21\/nourish-bloom-market-first-black-owned-autonomous-grocery-opens-in-atlanta\/\">Nourish + Bloom Market<\/a> that opened in January. In that article, we pointed out that the store was entering territory that included <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/02\/25\/amazon-opens-its-first-cashierless-grocery-store\/\">Amazon Go<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/02\/06\/7-eleven-is-the-next-retailer-to-test-cashierless-stores\/\">7-Eleven<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/12\/10\/walmart-partners-with-self-driving-startup-nuro-to-test-autonomous-grocery-delivery-in-houston\/\">Walmart<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Behind some of that cashierless technology are startup companies like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/27\/look-out-amazon-go-a-lisbon-startup-plans-to-offer-autonomous-stores-to-other-retailers\/\">Sensei<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/10\/10\/autonomous-retail\/\">Standard Cognition<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.getzippin.com\/\">Zippin<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/grabango.com\/\">Grabango<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.trigo.tech\/\">Trigo<\/a>, which all recently took in venture capital to advance their approaches.<\/p>\n<p>The latest company with an injection of VC is <a href=\"http:\/\/www.aifi.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">AiFi<\/a>, which enables retailers to deploy and scale autonomous shopping cost-effectively. It does this in grocery stores, sport stadiums and convenience stores via a camera-only resource that does not require weighted shelves, significantly decreasing the cost and time it takes to get up-and-running, co-founder and CEO Steve Gu said.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2283207\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>In addition, its advanced tracking algorithms work in up to 10,000 square feet of space to support various shopping methods, including an app, credit card, gated or hybrid entry.<\/p>\n<p>Santa Clara-based AiFi raised $65 million in Series B funding with participation from retail partners Aldi, Zabka and Verizon Ventures, which is enabling the company to utilize 5G technology.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Zlkz86qzOv\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/02\/27\/aifi-emerges-from-stealth-with-its-own-take-on-cashier-free-retail-similar-to-amazon-go\/\">AiFi emerges from stealth with its own take on cashier-free retail, similar to Amazon Go<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;AiFi emerges from stealth with its own take on cashier-free retail, similar to Amazon Go&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/02\/27\/aifi-emerges-from-stealth-with-its-own-take-on-cashier-free-retail-similar-to-amazon-go\/embed\/#?secret=daMhQS6KB7#?secret=Zlkz86qzOv\" data-secret=\"Zlkz86qzOv\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span class=\"embed-youtube embed breakout embed--video\" style=\"text-align:center; display: block;\"><iframe class=\"youtube-player\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/embed\/YXBKqn8PJvM?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;fs=1&#038;hl=en-US&#038;autohide=2&#038;wmode=transparent\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" style=\"border:0;\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts allow-same-origin allow-popups allow-presentation\"><\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>This round gives the company a total of $80 million in funding and comes four years after we reported on <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/02\/27\/aifi-emerges-from-stealth-with-its-own-take-on-cashier-free-retail-similar-to-amazon-go\/\">AiFi emerging from stealth<\/a> and two years after it took in what Gu had called its \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/qualcomm-backed-aifi-to-deploy-14-5m-in-autonomous-stores\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">pre-Series B<\/a>.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>He intends to use the new funding to strengthen the company\u2019s deployment team in order to launch stores faster and more efficiently. On that front, Gu believes AiFi has cracked the formula: in 2020, it would take six months to get a store ready to accept customers, and the company is now able to reduce that to less than one week.<\/p>\n<p>In addition, AiFi will invest in product development and feature enhancement.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cAutonomous checkout is just the beginning,\u201d he said. \u201cFrom the data we are getting, people are starting to see the way you manage an autonomous store is similar to an e-commerce website.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The capital infusion comes at a time when AiFi is experiencing growth. Two years ago, the company had no public-facing stores, and now it has 40 stores, including 30 with Zabka. Back then its largest store was 3,000 square feet, and in January, it launched a 6,000-square-foot Aldi store in London.<\/p>\n<p>Last November, AiFi went live in Paris with a first-of-its-kind, 10\/10 Flash concept store with Carrefour. It expanded to National Football League stadiums and music festivals, where stores have reduced average transaction and queue time by 50% and increased per capita sales by 170%.<\/p>\n<p>In addition to Aldi, Carrefour and Zabka, which Gu pointed out currently has the highest number of autonomous stores around the world powered by computer vision, AiFi is also working with Compass Group to open Market x Flutter, Ireland\u2019s first completely frictionless store.<\/p>\n<p>All of that movement has resulted in revenue growth of five to six times year over year, and the need for AiFi to increase its headcount from 40 employees in 2020 to 115 people all over the world today.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Gu mentioned the global pandemic was a factor in helping retailers and consumers realize the importance of autonomous stores. On the retail side, it was also a benefit, as stores struggled to hire people.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"7juzvr9dGc\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/29\/4-views-on-the-future-of-retail-the-check-out-process-and-lines\/\">4 views on the future of retail and the shopping experience<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;4 views on the future of retail and the shopping experience&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/29\/4-views-on-the-future-of-retail-the-check-out-process-and-lines\/embed\/#?secret=JIKyjMBSab#?secret=7juzvr9dGc\" data-secret=\"7juzvr9dGc\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Labor shortages resulting from the \u201cThe Great Resignation\u201d was actually the second wave that hurt retailers, the first being people not going into stores because they didn\u2019t want to touch things in the store, Melody Brue, retail technology analyst at Moor Insights, said.<\/p>\n<p>She concurs with AiFi\u2019s data from pilot phases of stores reducing checkout time and increasing purchase volume. In addition, it enables smaller stores to keep more accurate inventory that results in better management of the supply chain.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are getting so much data about how a customer shops, in what parts of the store people buy more and what products sell the best,\u201d Brue said. \u201cThere is a lot of intelligence from this type of shopping that would take longer for a typical store manager to gather. If chips are selling better in aisle two than aisle four, that might be harder to recognize.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>With regard to continued funding into the autonomous retail space, it still seems to be flowing, as evidenced by AiFi and some additional companies, including French convenience store startup <a href=\"https:\/\/www.pymnts.com\/news\/investment-tracker\/2022\/boxy-expands-its-network-of-autonomous-convenience-stores-with-28m-raise\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Boxy<\/a>, which announced $28 million in funding a few weeks ago, and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/focal-systems-raises-25-8m-in-series-b-funding-to-automate-retail-globally-301450812.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Focal Systems<\/a>, which works with retailers like Walmart. In December, it raised $25.8 million for its retail automation.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe\u2019ve definitely seen big investments into automation, artificial intelligence and retail, and in some ways, it had a fintech element to it,\u201d Brue said. \u201cIt looks like there has been a little bit of a dip-in-and-wait, for example, AiFi\u2019s initial funding was a small round, and now it is getting a much bigger tranche. Venture capital investment over the past couple of years has been thematic in that way of investing in areas that add convenience and efficiency into people\u2019s lives, and from a financial and retail perspective, that is getting a lot of traction.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"8J5Ws4cZ79\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/01\/whos-building-the-grocery-store-of-the-future\/\">Who&#8217;s building the grocery store of the future?<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Who&#8217;s building the grocery store of the future?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/01\/whos-building-the-grocery-store-of-the-future\/embed\/#?secret=gmgHKf19PH#?secret=8J5Ws4cZ79\" data-secret=\"8J5Ws4cZ79\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Contactless stores are gaining traction, more so in Europe, but there are some trickling into the U.S., including Atlanta\u2019s Nourish + Bloom Market that opened in January. In that article, we pointed out that the store was entering territory that included Amazon Go, 7-Eleven and Walmart.
