Group","slug":"compass-group","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449554479"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449554479"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449554479"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449554479"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449554479"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557099,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/europe\/","name":"Europe","slug":"europe","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557099"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557099"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557099"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557099"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557099"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2283042,"date":"2022-03-11T05:03:47","date_gmt":"2022-03-11T13:03:47","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2283042"},"modified":"2022-03-10T12:15:33","modified_gmt":"2022-03-10T20:15:33","slug":"aument-wants-to-power-your-next-marketing-message","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/11\/aument-wants-to-power-your-next-marketing-message\/","title":{"rendered":"Aument wants to power your next marketing message"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https:\/\/aument.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Aument<\/a> is carving out a niche in marketing automation for e-commerce stores, raising $1.5 million in pre-seed funding just four months after being founded.<\/p>\n<p>CEO Emilio Di Marco met his co-founders, Alan Helouani, Sacha Landesmann and Mario Leon Rojas, in Latin America while leading marketing efforts for WeWork. Their experience in working on customer acquisition and retention was the ultimate driver for Aument.<\/p>\n<p>They founded the company in November 2021 and launched the product in February, which is using data science and automation marketing to help e-commerce stories, currently selling via Shopify, to acquire and retain more customers.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2283042\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cFew companies can take advantage of the data they have,\u201d Di Marco told TechCrunch. \u201cThey can\u2019t hire talented data scientists or growth marketers to put their data into relevant communications.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Miami-based Aument is building a library of actions, taking e-commerce best practices and automating them for small businesses to start sending automated and personalized marketing messages and convert visitors to customers. It\u2019s something Di Marco calls \u201ce-commerce marketing management-as-a-service,\u201d a mouthful indeed.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"FP84hCbhLb\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/stop-guessing-your-kpis-varos-shows-e-commerce-saas-companies-how-you-compare-to-peers\/\">Stop guessing your KPIs; Varos shows e-commerce, SaaS companies how you compare to peers<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Stop guessing your KPIs; Varos shows e-commerce, SaaS companies how you compare to peers&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/stop-guessing-your-kpis-varos-shows-e-commerce-saas-companies-how-you-compare-to-peers\/embed\/#?secret=YNOx6oVMqq#?secret=FP84hCbhLb\" data-secret=\"FP84hCbhLb\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2283045\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2283045\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2283045\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/2-New-Actions-Aument.png\" alt=\"Aument\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/2-New-Actions-Aument.png 1179w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/2-New-Actions-Aument.png?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/2-New-Actions-Aument.png?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/2-New-Actions-Aument.png?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/2-New-Actions-Aument.png?resize=680,382 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/2-New-Actions-Aument.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2283045\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Aument<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Here\u2019s how it works: Once users install the app, they will see a screen with the library of actions. After clicking on an action, the user will see a set of goals, like audience and communication channels, and they plug in those actions and Aument starts running. Each of the actions have an attribution model behind it, so users can see how much revenue is coming back to the company and performance of the action.<\/p>\n<p>We\u2019ve been following other companies making a similar journey, most recently <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/04\/disco-gets-brands-to-boogie-together-on-customer-acquisition\/\">Disco<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/stop-guessing-your-kpis-varos-shows-e-commerce-saas-companies-how-you-compare-to-peers\/\">Varos<\/a>, which are also developing tools that aim to keep customer acquisition costs down. The <a href=\"https:\/\/www.huntclub.com\/blog\/average-customer-acquisition-cost#:~:text=Average%20customer%20acquisition%20based%20on%20industries&amp;text=Retail%3A%20%2410,Transportation%3A%20%2498\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cost depends on the industry<\/a>, while the <a href=\"https:\/\/hbr.org\/2014\/10\/the-value-of-keeping-the-right-customers#:~:text=If%20you're%20not%20convinced,the%20right%20customers%20is%20valuable.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Harvard Business Review<\/a> reported the cost of acquiring a new customer can average five to 25 times higher than retaining one.<\/p>\n<p>Others point out that determining this in e-commerce is tricky \u2014 something Varos is specifically working on \u2014 but that small businesses might pay around $20 per new customer, while it&#8217;s more like $160 for Amazon.<\/p>\n<p>At the same time, HBR also reported that a 5% bump in customer retention can mean increased profits of 25%. That definitely can mean a lot for the more than 8 million online stores that Di Marco estimates are live around the world, and selling through marketplaces, including Shopify, WooCommerce and Magento. Their combined sales topped $5 trillion this year, and are poised to grow to $7 trillion by 2025, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.emarketer.com\/content\/worldwide-ecommerce-continues-double-digit-growth-following-pandemic-push-online\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according to eMarketer<\/a>.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Where Di Marco says Aument is different is in its ability to reduce time between the first and second purchase, while also activating customers at risk of not coming back. He believes the company\u2019s \u201csecret sauce\u201d is that customers need to solve the jobs to be done to drive more sales and retention, not the sending part.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cTraditional players are extending service in more automated ways like Klaviyo or Twilio, which are our direct competitors,\u201d he added. \u201cIn sending, they are doing a great job. What we see when we analyze those products is that we see a lot of \u2018Photoshops,\u2019 but no \u2018Canva\u2019 there, so we are trying to build the Canva of this industry.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Aument mostly has a technical team currently and wants to hire additional talent in development and its core business, which the new pre-seeding funding will go toward. It was led by Expa and by The Rising Tide Network. Other investors include Hive Hatch, Matterscale Ventures, H20, Newtopia, Latitud and a group of individual investors, like Francisco Alvarez-Demalde, co-founder and managing partner of Riverwood Capital.<\/p>\n<p>The company is pre-revenue and started with 20 active stores and 40 on the waitlist. Di Marco says it is still in beta, but already has customers that want to pay to use the service and will work on building that out in the coming weeks.<\/p>\n<p>Up next, Aument will be heads down in the first and second quarters with additional users to test the product, and figure out its strategy to increase the library of actions, product and commercial integrations with Shopify while also adding new ones, like WooCommerce, third-party checkout and subscription applications.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"CZzppcZSqp\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/06\/after-talking-to-marketing-leaders-for-a-year-heres-my-advice-for-ceos\/\">After talking to marketing leaders for a year, here&#8217;s my advice for CEOs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;After talking to marketing leaders for a year, here&#8217;s my advice for CEOs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/06\/after-talking-to-marketing-leaders-for-a-year-heres-my-advice-for-ceos\/embed\/#?secret=WQ3hz98bP6#?secret=CZzppcZSqp\" data-secret=\"CZzppcZSqp\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Aument is carving out a niche in marketing automation for e-commerce stores, raising $1.5 million in pre-seed funding just four months after being founded. CEO Emilio Di Marco met his co-founders, Alan Helouani, Sacha Landesmann and Mario Leon Rojas, in Latin America while leading marketing efforts for WeWork. Their experience in working on customer acquisition Rojas","slug":"mario-leon-rojas","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576993179"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576993179"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576993179"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576993179"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576993179"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":175,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/marketing\/","name":"Marketing","slug":"marketing","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/175"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=175"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=175"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=175"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=175"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2282413,"date":"2022-03-10T07:00:27","date_gmt":"2022-03-10T15:00:27","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2282413"},"modified":"2022-03-10T11:55:44","modified_gmt":"2022-03-10T19:55:44","slug":"new-stack-ventures-raises-second-fund-focused-on-silicon-valley-outsiders","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/10\/new-stack-ventures-raises-second-fund-focused-on-silicon-valley-outsiders\/","title":{"rendered":"New Stack Ventures raises second fund focused on Silicon Valley outsiders"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Early-stage venture fund <a href=\"https:\/\/www.newstack.vc\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">New Stack Ventures<\/a> just raised $42.6 million for its second fund aimed at injecting capital into founders that don\u2019t come from the educational pedigree or location that we typically see with entrepreneurs.<\/p>\n<p>Touting itself as one of the \u201clargest single-partner U.S. funds ever raised between the coasts,\u201d the Chicago-based firm prides itself on being unique from other venture capital firms, and that stems from the founder and general partner Nick Moran, who previously worked for Danaher in M&amp;A and product management, where he developed an analytical device for testing compounds in drinking water.<\/p>\n<p>When Moran began angel investing, he found the whole process of startup fundraising to be confusing, so he started a venture podcast back in May 2014 called \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/fullratchet.net\/about\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Full Ratchet<\/a>,\u201d to interview other VCs and provide funding transparency.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2282413\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>New Stack raised its first fund of $6 million in 2018 and has since gone on to add 38 companies to its portfolio, including Hologram, Cybrary, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/10\/fairmarkit-lands-30m-series-b-to-modernize-procurement\/\">Fairmarkit<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/06\/02\/chicagos-tovala-gobbles-up-20m-for-its-smart-ovenmeal-kit-service\/\">Tovala<\/a>. It makes angel, pre-seed and seed investments into B2B SaaS startups in sectors like finance, healthcare, cybersecurity, supply chain, construction and real estate.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"LtDhIGTg5M\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/06\/02\/chicagos-tovala-gobbles-up-20m-for-its-smart-ovenmeal-kit-service\/\">Tovala gobbles up $20M for its smart oven+meal kit service<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Tovala gobbles up $20M for its smart oven+meal kit service&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/06\/02\/chicagos-tovala-gobbles-up-20m-for-its-smart-ovenmeal-kit-service\/embed\/#?secret=gIpkanh9Ix#?secret=LtDhIGTg5M\" data-secret=\"LtDhIGTg5M\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>I spoke with Moran about how the firm\u2019s focus between the coasts and how investments there have evolved. The following was edited for clarity and length.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: The current portfolio is largely enterprise\/B2B, with a few notable investments in food tech. Why are those areas attractive to you?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>NM: I come from the B2B enterprise world, so about 75% of our portfolio is enterprise SaaS. When I got back to Chicago and was an angel investor, people weren&#8217;t focused on some potential unicorns and didn&#8217;t invest in areas like food tech or social commerce, which have become breakout successes. We didn&#8217;t start with a thesis there, but due to lack of capital and networks in the Midwest, we had our choice of backing those founders.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: It looks like you were looking in between the coasts a bit before it was popular. What were the initial challenges?\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>NM: A lot of ingredients have to come together for it to work &#8212; a founder network, a talent network and a capital network. Raising the first fund, the thesis of investing in outsiders and the middle of the country was a difficult task. We just closed the second raise, and the thesis landed, and we have 100 investors and people who are motivated and excited. We think the bigger story is the migration of Midwesterners back to the Midwest who had to locate in the Bay Area for work. That has been a huge tailwind for us.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><strong>TC: How have those ingredients improved?\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>NM: The capital and talent networks are now robust, especially with remote work. We still have to go to the coasts when it comes to Series A and Series B, but more coastal investors are embracing Midwest founders. At the seed stage, it is initially hard, but once you get the traction and investors to see the value, we have seen the appetite for investing in our companies. We are starting to see our portfolio companies raise Series B and Series C rounds, and our first D round is coming up. Those would not have happened for Midwest companies when I first started, but now with tech, you can find networks everywhere.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: How many companies are you looking to invest in with fund 2?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>NM: This one will be 35 investments, with average check sizes increasing from $400,000 to $1 million.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: Diversity is paramount in venture capital, in both the firm itself and the companies in the portfolio. How is your firm addressing diversity?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>NM: An important part of our outsider thesis includes those that have been marginalized or underrepresented. The founders of our portfolio companies are helping to break the traditional stereotypes in tech. I&#8217;ve learned in hosting \u201cThe Full Ratchet\u201d that more diverse teams outperform those that are less so. We are excited to announce some new hires to our core team in the coming months that will help us embrace and promote gender and racial diversity in venture capital. In order to help &#8220;young outsiders&#8221; break into venture capital, in 2020 we launched the New Stack Fellowship. The graduates of this program were 58% women and 85% underrepresented, and many have gone on to full-time jobs or internships in VC and tech. This group drove material impact for New Stack, and we look forward to teaching and benefiting from the next generation of great investors.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: Why should founders want you in their cap table?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>NM: From the beginning, the venture capital industry has chronically lacked innovation. They used to investing\u00a0in the same kind of industry and\u00a0the same type of\u00a0person, but we are seeing a future where this is\u00a0changing. We are innovating with our podcast, where we have founders reaching out to us. If you ask founders why they chose us, in the Midwest, most\u00a0other\u00a0VC firms know analysts or associates at all of the Series A firms. But very few know founding partners and general partners at 90% of the Tier 1 Series A and B firms.\u00a0We can claim that because we have been interviewing them and building relationships. Founders want access to decision-makers, and we provide that warm on-ramp to firms on the coasts.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"qhZPUoybcM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/19\/when-vcs-turned-to-zoom-chicago-startups-were-ready-for-their-close-up\/\">When VCs turned to Zoom, Chicago startups were ready for their close-up<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, ags=576603458"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576603458"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":1417,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/money\/","name":"money","slug":"money","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/1417"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=1417"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=1417"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=1417"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=1417"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576992834,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/new-stack-ventures\/","name":"New Stack Ventures","slug":"new-stack-ventures","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576992834"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576992834"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576992834"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576992834"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576992834"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2282283,"date":"2022-03-10T05:03:18","date_gmt":"2022-03-10T13:03:18","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2282283"},"modified":"2022-03-10T06:57:41","modified_gmt":"2022-03-10T14:57:41","slug":"topsort-an-auction-based-advertising-startup-now-valued-at-110m-after-seed-round","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/10\/topsort-an-auction-based-advertising-startup-now-valued-at-110m-after-seed-round\/","title":{"rendered":"Topsort, an auction-based advertising startup, now valued at $110M after seed round"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">When Regina Ye was in college, she was a Shopify seller and recalls being so fed up with advertising solutions that she spent finals week staying up late to figure out how ads worked on Facebook and Amazon.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt was super complicated,\u201d she told TechCrunch. \u201cI was an early adopter of B2B marketplaces, but advertising was this black box. I didn\u2019t realize how much I would have to do this as a seller.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>There were two things that frustrated her: one was the complex structure of monetizing those channels effectively, and the other was the lack of direct promotional tools made available by the retail channels she was selling through, which she thought would be both less saturated and competitive than Facebook and Google.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2282283\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>During her time as product lead at Hopin Ye met Stanford professor Michael Ostrovsky, who is an expert in marketplace design and auction theory, and Francisco Larrain, a serial entrepreneur who had an early exit to Groupon and led its engineering.<\/p>\n<p>As more marketplaces are affected by the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/04\/on-metas-regulatory-headwinds-and-adtechs-privacy-reckoning\/\">shift to user privacy<\/a>, the group took a look at how to innovate in this space without dealing with privacy. Exploring Ostrovsky\u2019s work on auctions, together they started <a href=\"https:\/\/www.topsort.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Topsort<\/a> in 2021 to provide auction-based advertising technology, through APIs, so that smaller retailers and vendors could more easily promote without the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/04\/where-will-our-data-go-when-cookies-disappear\/\">reliance on cookies, which are poised to go away<\/a>.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"HJWe38K9mA\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/04\/where-will-our-data-go-when-cookies-disappear\/\">Where will our data go when cookies disappear?<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Where will our data go when cookies disappear?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/04\/where-will-our-data-go-when-cookies-disappear\/embed\/#?secret=3oF4LSiDtc#?secret=HJWe38K9mA\" data-secret=\"HJWe38K9mA\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Their approach is retail media technology for small businesses to use auctions as a way to create effective advertising. When the user installs the API, they can start a campaign, including sponsored listings, banner ads and video ads, and are able to control how ads are shown, how ad quality and relevance are measured and who can launch campaigns. Larrain says the auctions run in as little as 20 milliseconds at 10,000 requests per second.<\/p>\n<p>When considering how much to bid for clicks, Topsort provides suggestions using its proprietary algorithm to maximize clicks and conversions. It also has an auto-bidding feature for cost-per-click ads so that vendors can input a budget and time period, and the company will take it from there. Ye said it can guarantee between two times and four times in returns depending on the marketplace.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI don\u2019t agree that ads should be a guessing game,\u201d Ye added. \u201cThis is very much a clean way of doing advertising, and we fill the gap with no privacy data, but math and machine learning. What sets us apart is how easy it is, which is why advertising technology has traditionally had a bad rep.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Topsort has gained most of its customers in the past four months, and some of them are already bringing in $1 million to $15 billion in gross merchandise value.<\/p>\n<p>One of its early customers is <a href=\"https:\/\/www.topsort.com\/post\/how-a-15m-gmv-chilean-baby-e-commerce-website-leveraged-promoted-listings-for-cyber-monday\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Babytuto<\/a>, a parent and baby product retailer in Chile that initially worked with the company for Cyber Monday. Based on achieving a 40% vendor adoption rate, Topsort reported in its case study that \u201cbased on the vendor activity, the performance of this batch of sponsored listings, and the marketplace characteristics, our projection is that promoted listings on Babytuto will eventually generate additional profit equal to approximately 5% of their gross merchandise value.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Ye says the company has learned a lot from Babytuto and its dozens of other early customers so far, including Yummy, Facily, Airlift and Chiper, and wants to accelerate growth and scale its go-to-market strategy.<\/p>\n<p>The company raised $8 million in seed funding that values the company at a whopping $110 million. The round includes investment from marketplace investors including Pear Ventures, Quiet Capital, FJLabs, Micky Malka (Ribbit Capital), Lydia Jett (SoftBank), Akhil Paul, Comma VC and a group of individual investors.<\/p>\n<p>Ye and Larrain say the new funding will go into growing a sales and marketing team and deepen the footprint Topsort has in Latin American and Asia.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are hitting a point where we have gone from zero to one, and all of the investors doubled down,\u201d Ye said. \u201cWe\u2019ve hit our customers in their ramp-up, but we would love to be there earlier. This area is so misunderstood, and we want to do more user education and come up with different ranges of products to also help smaller marketplaces get started as we work with all marketplaces at a different scale.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"tBJnKLbZ9h\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/08\/26\/how-to-use-amazon-and-advertising-to-build-a-d2c-startup\/\">How to use Amazon and advertising to build a D2C startup<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;How to use Amazon and advertising to build a D2C startup&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/08\/26\/how-to-use-amazon-and-advertising-to-build-a-d2c-startup\/embed\/#?secret=e06TGfWIjO#?secret=tBJnKLbZ9h\" data-secret=\"tBJnKLbZ9h\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>When Jett","slug":"lydia-jett","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576919744"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576919744"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576919744"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576919744"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576919744"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":40978,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/machine-learning\/","name":"machine learning","slug":"machine-learning","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/40978"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=40978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=40978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=40978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=40978"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2281803,"date":"2022-03-09T06:05:45","date_gmt":"2022-03-09T14:05:45","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2281803"},"modified":"2022-03-09T08:09:28","modified_gmt":"2022-03-09T16:09:28","slug":"s3-ventures-tacora-austin-startups","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/09\/s3-ventures-tacora-austin-startups\/","title":{"rendered":"S3 Ventures, Tacora close on new funds to boost Austin startups"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Austin\u2019s venture capital scene has been hot for years now, but a pair of local investment firms just closed on new funds aimed at injecting more capital into startups in Austin and elsewhere.<\/p>\n<p>One is <a href=\"https:\/\/www.s3vc.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">S3 Ventures<\/a>, a venture capital firm that\u2019s been around since 2005, which raised $250 million for its Fund VII, touting itself as \u201cthe largest venture capital fund focused on Texas-based startups.\u201d The other is a new player in the ecosystem, Tacora, which announced the first close \u2014 $250 million \u2014 of its debut fund, which is targeting $300 million, to provide asset-based lending to venture-backed companies.<\/p>\n<p>More than <a href=\"https:\/\/www.axios.com\/local\/austin\/2022\/01\/14\/austin-venture-capital-funding-startups\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">380 funding deals were made into Austin startups in 2021<\/a>, amounting to $4.9 billion, which is a record for the city, according to PitchBook data. Axios reported that this was 211% over the number of dollars invested in 2020. \u200b<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281803\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>While that still puts the city behind the investment meccas of the Bay Area, New York, Boston and Los Angeles, Austin is proving it can hold its own in attracting not only startup companies, but also large corporations like Oracle, Apple, HP and Tesla, as well as <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/11\/austin-transplant-geoff-lewis-wants-to-pop-silicon-valleys-self-referential-bubble\/\">Silicon Valley investors<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Brian Smith was an early believer in the city, founding S3 Ventures with a $20 million first fund after a career as an electrical engineer at companies like IBM before starting his own company, Crossroads Systems. The firm has eight investors, including general partner Charlie Plauche, partner Eric Engineer and principal Aaron Perman.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"3lLGlzMxzy\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/09\/6-vcs-talk-the-future-of-austins-exploding-startup-ecosystem\/\">6 VCs talk the future of Austin&#8217;s exploding startup ecosystem<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;6 VCs talk the future of Austin&#8217;s exploding startup ecosystem&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/09\/6-vcs-talk-the-future-of-austins-exploding-startup-ecosystem\/embed\/#?secret=CoLMQRnU02#?secret=3lLGlzMxzy\" data-secret=\"3lLGlzMxzy\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWhile building a company here between 1994 and 2003, I saw the Texas ecosystem firsthand and was excited about what it offered,\u201d Smith told TechCrunch. \u201cIt was a great place to live and work, and I believed that over time, it would be a growing venture opportunity.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>In fact, the firm believes that Texas is going to be the second-largest tech ecosystem in the U.S. by 2030, something <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/09\/6-vcs-talk-the-future-of-austins-exploding-startup-ecosystem\/\">Engineer alluded to in another TechCrunch interview<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Here, he reiterated that a demographic shift was happening, and as many of the top fastest-growing large metropolitan areas are in Texas, tech corporations are opening headquarters or second headquarters across the state &#8212; and an influx of talent is following.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe&#8217;re constantly meeting entrepreneurs that are at the frontier of things because they&#8217;re running into technology issues that others don&#8217;t have,\u201d Engineer added. \u201cThey&#8217;re the ones innovating, so we believe that big trend is going to be the driver, more than anything.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>S3 Ventures has been backed by one limited partner for the entirety of its history, a family with a multibillion-dollar foundation focused on addressing social inequities. Smith, Plauche and Engineer say this enables them more time to look for good companies, not to have to sell a company to raise a new fund and only have to update one investor.<\/p>\n<p>The investment thesis will be the same with Fund VII, with the firm focusing on investing at the seed, Series A and Series B stages in business technology, digital experiences and healthcare technology companies. They expect to invest in 25 companies, also similar to previous funds.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The firm has invested in more than 50 companies and saw over 20 exits so far, including digital banking fintech company <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/05\/digging-into-the-alkami-technology-ipo\/\">Alkami Technology, which went public last year<\/a>, and construction payment company <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/12\/19\/levelset-raises-30-million-to-improve-money-management-for-contractors-in-construction\/\">Levelset<\/a>, which was acquired by Procore Technologies.<\/p>\n<p>What is different is that with a larger fund, they can deploy the capital faster than in previous funds, Plauche said. Historically, the firm invested in about four companies, but last year that figure doubled.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281985\" style=\"width: 410px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281985\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2281985\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Keri-Findley-e1646833138336.jpg\" alt=\"Keri Findley, Tacora\" width=\"400\" height=\"400\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Keri-Findley-e1646833138336.jpg 638w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Keri-Findley-e1646833138336.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Keri-Findley-e1646833138336.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Keri-Findley-e1646833138336.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Keri-Findley-e1646833138336.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Keri-Findley-e1646833138336.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Keri-Findley-e1646833138336.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Keri-Findley-e1646833138336.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 400px) 100vw, 400px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281985\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Keri Findley, founder of Tacora<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, investment management firm <a href=\"http:\/\/www.tacoracap.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Tacora<\/a> was founded by Keri Findley in 2021. Previously, she ran the structured credit portfolio for investment adviser Third Point. She recalls over a decade ago talking to tech-enabled consumer lenders about how technology would affect financial services.<\/p>\n<p>Fast-forward to today, and we have fintech, insurtech, proptech, logistics and transportation, all capital-intensive businesses that Tacora is focused on. The firm, which is geographically agnostic, can help with funding their assets; for example, houses, options on real estate and regulatory capital often used by insurtech companies.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cNew businesses need more complex capital than they are raising,\u201d Findley said. \u201cWe are focused on anyone who has intended \u2014 those they knew they were going to originate \u2014 or unintended assets, like if you have a company that builds a robot, and you suddenly need to have inventory, it needs to be financed with a different type of capital other than venture equity and debt.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"n0rMRe4Evv\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/05\/digging-into-the-alkami-technology-ipo\/\">Digging into the Alkami Technology IPO<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Digging into the Alkami Technology IPO&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/05\/digging-into-the-alkami-technology-ipo\/embed\/#?secret=tKGB6OBL13#?secret=n0rMRe4Evv\" data-secret=\"n0rMRe4Evv\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Tacora\u2019s fund is backed by prominent venture capitalist Peter Thiel, whose Mithril Capital Management, an investment firm he co-founded with Ajay Royan, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/09\/21\/mithril-capital-management-cofounded-by-ajay-royan-and-peter-thiel-is-leaving-the-bay-area\/\">left the Bay Area for Austin in 2018<\/a>. Later, Royan <a href=\"https:\/\/finance.yahoo.com\/news\/happened-mithril-peter-thiel-wasn-100007775.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">ran into a bit of controversy a year later<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Findley met Thiel when she started looking at venture-backed companies and figuring out the players in the space. When she was learning about those funding interesting businesses or who was on the cutting edge of technology changes in her target sectors, Thiel was in every one of those conversations, she said.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI got to know him through that process,\u201d Findley added. \u201cLast year, when I was talking about what we were doing, he offered to be the vehicle for the fund. I am happy to have him as a partner.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>In addition to the capital, which utilizes a combination of equity, debt and other structured finance tools so that companies can scale assets and grow while minimizing dilution, companies will also have access to Tacora\u2019s strategic network.<\/p>\n<p>Tacora has signed some term sheets already, but is going through the regulatory due diligence process, Findley said. She is confident that some of them will convert to funding.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are here to help early-stage companies finance their assets,\u201d she said. \u201cThis is a complete white space where oftentimes entrepreneurs are confused and don\u2019t know how capital markets work. We help them walk through the process and provide flexible capital so they can grow without roadblocks.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"JcgeoGnnmf\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/14\/facebook-investor-jim-breyer-picks-austin-as-breyer-capitals-second-home\/\">Facebook investor Jim Breyer picks Austin as Breyer Capital&#8217;s second home<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook investor Jim Breyer picks Austin as Breyer Capital&#8217;s second home&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/14\/facebook-investor-jim-breyer-picks-austin-as-breyer-capitals-second-home\/embed\/#?secret=KUAC9ZoZzx#?secret=JcgeoGnnmf\" data-secret=\"JcgeoGnnmf\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Austin\u2019s venture capital scene has been hot for years now, but a pair of local investment firms just closed on new funds aimed at injecting more capital into startups in Austin and elsewhere. Katzenberg, WndrCo flex funding muscles with string of new deals"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">When you see Jeffrey Katzenberg\u2019s name associated with an investment, you take a look. However, when you see his name multiple times in your inbox, for example, tied to funding rounds for Sparrow, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/real-time-flight-rewards-search-engine-point-me-raises-2m-to-scale-its-travel-tool\/\">Point.me<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/24\/jeffrey-katzenberg-backs-the-10m-seed-round-for-hubucs-embedded-finance-api\/\">HUBUC<\/a>, and one I personally wrote about last week, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/04\/popchew-creator-food-brands\/\">Popchew<\/a>, it\u2019s time to inquire what he has been up to.<\/p>\n<p>The famed DreamWorks SKG co-founder and former chairman of The Walt Disney Studios, Jeffrey Katzenberg is a founding partner, with Sujay Jaswa, at <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wndrco.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">WndrCo<\/a>, a holding company that acquires, operates and develops businesses at the intersection of technology and media.<\/p>\n<p>Jaswa was a principal at New Enterprise Associates before joining Dropbox as one of the company\u2019s early employees. The two met years ago when Katzenberg was looking for his next big thing, which he wanted to be \u201ccompletely new and different.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281679\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The last time I had heard his name could have been the same time you did: when <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/10\/21\/quibi-is-dead\/\">Quibi\u2019s streaming service came to a screeching halt in October 2020<\/a>, mere months after it launched.<\/p>\n<p>Katzenberg declined to address questions concerning how Quibi&#8217;s failure impacts his relationship with founders and how it informs his investment decisions. He offered only that he&#8217;s &#8220;very proud of my failure &#8212; I own it.&#8221; But he talked at length about some of his current bets and what drew him to them. My chat with Katzenberg and Jaswa follows, edited for length.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"n5kWORlpEr\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/real-time-flight-rewards-search-engine-point-me-raises-2m-to-scale-its-travel-tool\/\">Real-time flight rewards search engine point.me raises $2M to scale its travel tool<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Real-time flight rewards search engine point.me raises $2M to scale its travel tool&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/real-time-flight-rewards-search-engine-point-me-raises-2m-to-scale-its-travel-tool\/embed\/#?secret=0MeePP5Szy#?secret=n5kWORlpEr\" data-secret=\"n5kWORlpEr\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><strong>TC: How did you meet Sujay?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>JK: I met with 300 people, and he was the most interesting, smartest and all-around great person of everyone I met. I spent nine months every day, talking to people, spending time in northern California, seeing who was doing interesting stuff. Not everyone was a potential partner or available, but it was just part of my learning process of trying to find the right partner. Sujay\u2019s name just kept coming up in so many different places in so many different ways. When we finally did get together, he sort of exceeded expectations.<\/p>\n<p>Partnerships are no different than marriages: you know who they are, you know when you find somebody you think is compatible. And, you think your goals and values and ambitions are going to be the same, and you know it&#8217;s always a bit of a roll of the dice in life. Here we are five or six years later, and it could not have been a better outcome. I&#8217;m grateful that I found somebody who&#8217;s half my age and twice as smart as me.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: Going back to 2017, I was reading some articles about the founding of WndrCo. Were you an angel investor before starting the firm?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>JK: No, I would say the investments I had were more relationship-driven. I had a handful of these investments, but they were really driven by people that I had come to me that went out and started companies and that was my connection more than I had some investing thesis that I was doing.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><strong>TC: What ultimately sparked your curiosity for venture capital?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>JK: I think the investing side of it is really the smaller part of what we&#8217;re doing. It&#8217;s a sort of the company-building part of it that has been the most interesting to me and the one where I think I am probably spending more time.<\/p>\n<p>SJ: One of the things that&#8217;s very different about us is we think and act like founders every day, as opposed to just investors. We call ourselves \u201cthe founders behind the founders.\u201d For us, it&#8217;s super fun and we know it&#8217;s going to be a lot of work. Half of our money goes into those companies and the other half of the capital goes into the traditional product-market-fit kind of investing. Then we&#8217;ve now got a separate fund that actually does venture investing. It\u2019s seed investing and run by a cool rock star named Anthony (Saleh), who&#8217;s really one of the best seed investors.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: Several of your portfolio companies announced investments from you recently, including Sparrow, which manages employee leaves; Point.me, a reward travel booking company; and HUBUC, which focuses on embedded fintech. This is an eclectic batch of companies. What attracts you to certain companies over others?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>SJ: The common thread across everything is that we&#8217;re really looking for founders that we think have a chance of cracking an important problem.<\/p>\n<p>JK: I always looked at things that I can relate to as a consumer myself. Having been sort of in the direct-to-consumer business my whole life, I always light up at those ideas. We also look at companies that I think can make a meaningful contribution to the future of work. Sparrow is a particular pain point right now, and the importance of care and the value of how companies engage and look after their employees has literally gone through the roof.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"7cWmrE9d3o\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/24\/jeffrey-katzenberg-backs-the-10m-seed-round-for-hubucs-embedded-finance-api\/\">Jeffrey Katzenberg backs the $10M seed round for HUBUC&#8217;s embedded finance API<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Jeffrey Katzenberg backs the $10M seed round for HUBUC&#8217;s embedded finance API&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/24\/jeffrey-katzenberg-backs-the-10m-seed-round-for-hubucs-embedded-finance-api\/embed\/#?secret=xVjriyBmkP#?secret=7cWmrE9d3o\" data-secret=\"7cWmrE9d3o\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><strong>TC: What sectors are you not interested in?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>JK: We actually strategically made the decision to move away from digital media. I had interests in digital technology and used a fair amount of it in movie-making, but I wanted to do a hard pivot into a whole new world.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: With your kind of experiences, how have those helped inform the way you counsel founders?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>JK: Every founder has their unique challenges and opportunities. Just broadly, it&#8217;s the wisdom and experience of having done this for, in my case, four-plus decades, and having seen so many different opportunities and different companies founded and built. Some of that is incredibly valuable and timeless, and some of it is less relevant. I don&#8217;t know that there&#8217;s any one sort of magic pin now.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: What makes you a good strategic partner for a startup? Why should they choose you?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>SJ: The most important thing is that we&#8217;re founders, and we&#8217;re helping build companies every single day. Our experience isn&#8217;t from the past, it&#8217;s contemporaneous. We view it as there are four things that really matter for any company: product development, go-to-market, building and scaling the organization and capital. At this point, everyone has capital. What we try to do with the other three things is to offer a unique and distinctive value to these companies. And we&#8217;re not going to force any of it on you. Our job is just to be available for you to help you turbocharge on any of those things.<\/p>\n<p>JK: We don&#8217;t take board seats. We would rather get in there and get our hands dirty and actually problem-solve. More often than not, between Anthony, Sujay and myself, there&#8217;s always some value that we have to help, as Sujay put it, turbocharge these companies. It\u2019s also fun for us to see the result. The venture world has sort of done a pretty big pivot, and we&#8217;re just trying to find our own lane.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Vp7fblIyWb\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/15\/did-venture-capitalists-undervalue-startups-for-decades\/\">Did venture capitalists undervalue startups for
